§ 10.01 HOW CODE DESIGNATED AND CITED.
   The ordinances of the municipality of a general and permanent nature, as
codified and revised herein, are ordained as general ordinances and adopted as
“The Lost Creek Municipal Code,” hereinafter referred to as the “Town Code” or
“this code.”
(Ord. passed 10-2-1983)
§ 10.02 DEFINITIONS AND RULES OF CONSTRUCTION.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this code, the following definitions
shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different
meaning.
      COUNCIL or TOWN COUNCIL. The Council of the Town of Lost Creek, West
Virginia.
      COUNTY. The County of Harrison, West Virginia.
      FISCAL YEAR. The FISCAL YEAR for the town and all bodies or officers
collecting or disbursing funds shall begin on July 1 and expire with the
expiration of the next following June 30.
      FOLLOWING. The next after.
      MAY. The word MAY is permissive.
      MONTH. A calendar month.
      MUNICIPALITY. The Town of Lost Creek, West Virginia.
      OATH or SWORN. A solemn affirmation shall be the equivalent to an oath in
all cases unless otherwise expressly provided, and the word OATH shall be
deemed to include an affirmation, and the word SWEAR or SWORN to be complied
with if the person referred to makes solemn affirmation.
      OWNER. As applied to any property, any part owner, joint owner, tenant in
common, tenant in partnership, joint tenant or tenant by the entirety of the
whole or of a part of such property.
      PERSON. A corporation, firm, partnership, association, society, club or
any other group acting as a unit, as well as an individual unless restricted
within the context.
      PERSONAL PROPERTY. Goods and chattels, real and personal, money, credits,
investments and the evidence thereof.
      PRECEDING. The next before.
      PREMISES. When used as applicable to real property, shall include land
and buildings.
      PROPERTY. Real, personal and mixed property.
      REAL PROPERTY, REAL ESTATE, LAND or LANDS. Lands, buildings, tenements
and hereditaments, and all rights thereto and interests therein, except chattel
interests.
      REASONABLE TIME. In all cases where provision is made for an act to be
done or notice to be given within a REASONABLE TIME, it shall be construed to
mean only such time as may be necessary, under the circumstances then and there
existing, for the prompt performance of such act or the giving of such notice.
      SHALL. The word SHALL is mandatory.
      SIDEWALK. The portion of a street between the curbline or, where there is
no curb, the lateral lines of a roadway and the adjacent property line,
intended for the use of pedestrians. If there is no public area between the
lateral lines of the roadway and the abutting property line, then that area
immediately abutting the street line shall be considered a SIDEWALK AREA.
      SIGNATURE OR SUBSCRIPTION BY MARK. A mark made by a signer or subscriber
who cannot write, such signer’s or subscriber’s name being written near the
mark by a witness, who shall write his or her own name near the signer’s or
subscriber’s name.
      STATE. The State of West Virginia.
      STATE CODE. References to the State Code, or W. VA. Code, shall be to the
official West Virginia Code, as amended and currently in effect.
      STREET. An alley, avenue, boulevard, highway, road, lane, viaduct, bridge
and approaches thereto, and all other public thoroughfares in the town, and the
entire width thereof between abutting property lines; also, a sidewalk or
footpath unless the contrary is expressed or unless such construction would be
inconsistent with the intent of the Town Council.
      TENANT or OCCUPANT. Applied to a building or land, any person holding a
written or oral lease to or who occupies the whole or part of such building or
land, either alone or with others.
      TOWN. The Town of Lost Creek, West Virginia.
      TOWN CODE or THIS CODE. The code of the Town of Lost Creek, West
Virginia, as amended and currently in effect.
      YEAR. A calendar year. The word YEAR alone shall be equivalent to the
expression YEAR OF OUR LORD.
      WRITING. Includes any form of recorded message comprehensible by ordinary
visual means. Whenever any notice, report, statement or record is required or
authorized by this code or other ordinances or resolutions of the town, it
shall be made in writing in the English language unless it is expressly
provided otherwise.
   (B)   Rules of construction. In the construction of this code, the following
rules of construction shall be observed unless it shall be expressly provided
otherwise by any section, ordinance or resolution, unless inconsistent with the
manifest intent of the Town Council or unless the context clearly requires
otherwise.
      (1)   General interpretation. All general provisions, terms, phrases and
expressions shall be liberally construed in order that the true intent and
meaning of the Town Council may be fully carried out. Words and phrases shall
be taken in their usual sense, but technical words having a peculiar and
appropriate meaning in law shall be understood according to their technical
import.
      (2)   Officers, departments and the like. Officers, departments, boards,
commissions and employees referred to in this code shall mean officers,
departments, boards, commissions and employees of the town unless the content
clearly indicates otherwise.
      (3)   Authority of officers. Whenever authority is conferred on or an act
is required to be performed by a town officer, such authority may be exercised
or performed, at the instance of such officer, by a deputy, agent or
subordinate unless such authority cannot lawfully be deputed.
      (4)   Joint authority. All words giving a joint authority to three or
more persons or officers shall be construed as giving such joint authority to a
majority of such persons or officers and not to any lesser number.
      (5)   Gender. A word importing the masculine gender only may be construed
to include the feminine and neuter as well as the masculine.
      (6)   Number. A word importing the singular number only may be applied to
several persons or things as well as to one person or thing; a word importing
the plural number only may be applied to one person or thing as well as to
several.
      (7)   Tenses. The present tense includes the past and future tenses; the
future includes the present.
      (8)   Computation of time. The time within which an act is to be done
shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last, or, if the
last day is Sunday or a holiday, it shall also be excluded, but this provision
shall not be deemed to change any rule of law applicable to bills of exchange
or negotiable instruments; provided, that if time is expressed in hours, the
whole of any Sunday or holiday shall be excluded unless the clear intent of the
Town Council is to the contrary.
§ 10.03 CATCHLINES AND HEADINGS.
   The chapter, subchapter, section and division headings of this code are
intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents thereof and shall not be
deemed or taken to be titles thereof nor as any part thereof; nor, unless
expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of such chapters,
subchapters, sections or divisions, including the headings or catchlines, are
amended or reenacted.
Statutory reference:
   Construction of statutes, see W. Va. Code §§ 2-2-10(3) and 2-2-12
§ 10.04 PROVISIONS CONSIDERED AS CONTINUATIONS OF EXISTING ORDINANCES.
   Insofar as the provisions of this code are the same as those of ordinances
existing and in force at its effective date, said provisions shall be
considered to be continuations thereof and not as new enactments.
(Ord. passed 10-2-1983)
§ 10.05 ORDINANCES REPEALED.
   All ordinances of a general and permanent nature not contained in this code
are hereby repealed from and after the effective date of said code, except as
hereinafter provided.
(Ord. passed 10-2-1983)
§ 10.06 EFFECT OF REPEAL OF ORDINANCE.
   (A)   The repeal provided for in §
10.05 of this chapter shall not affect any offense or act committed or done, or
any penalty or forfeiture incurred, or any contract or right established or
accruing before the effective date of this code; nor shall such repeal affect
any ordinance or resolution promising or guaranteeing the payment of money for
the municipality, or authorizing the issuance of any bonds of said municipality
or any evidence of said municipality’s indebtedness, or any contract or
obligation assumed by said municipality; nor shall it affect any rights or
franchise conferred by any ordinance or resolution of the municipality or any
person, firm or corporation; nor shall it affect any prosecution, suit or other
proceeding pending or any judgment rendered on or prior to the effective date
of said code; nor shall it affect any ordinance annexing territory to the
municipality.
   (B)   When any ordinance which repealed another shall itself be repealed,
the previous ordinance shall not be revived without express words to that
effect.
(Ord. passed 10-2-1983)
Statutory reference:
   Effect of repeal or expiration of statutes, see W. Va. Code § 2-2-8
   Repeal of an act repealing a statute, see W. Va. Code § 2-2-9
§ 10.07 EFFECT OF REVISIONS.
   Immediately upon adoption of this code, it shall be reproduced in loose-leaf
form. The governing body, by motion or resolution, shall fix and change from
time to time, as considered necessary, the prices to be charged for copies of
this code and revisions thereto. After the adoption of this code, each general
ordinance shall be adopted as amending, adding or deleting a numbered section
or sections of said code; immediately thereafter, those affected pages of the
code shall be revised to reflect such amended, added or deleted material and
shall be distributed to town officers and employers having copies of said code
and to other persons who have requested and paid for current revisions. Notes
shall be inserted at the end of amended or new sections referring to the date
and number of ordinances making the amendments or adding the new sections, and
such references shall be cumulative if a section is amended more than once in
order that the current copy of this code will contain references to all
ordinances passed since the adoption of the original town code. One copy of
this code as originally adopted and one copy of each amending ordinance
thereafter adopted shall be mailed to the state’s Council of Towns and Cities
immediately upon final passage and adoption.
(Ord. passed 10-2-1983)
§ 10.08 SECTION HISTORIES; STATUTORY REFERENCES.
   (A)   As histories for the code sections, the specific number and passage
date of the original ordinance and amending ordinances, if any, are listed
following the text of the code section. Example:
(Ord. 10, passed 5-13-1960; Ord. 15, passed 1-1-1970; Ord. 20, passed 1-1-1980;
Ord. 25, passed 1-1-1985)
   (B)   (1)   If a statutory cite is included in the history, this indicates
that the text of the section reads substantially the same as the statute.
Example:
(W. Va. Code § 29B-1-1)
      (2)   If a statutory cite is set forth as a “statutory reference”
following the text of the section, this indicates that the reader should refer
to that statute for further information. Example:
§ 39.01 PUBLIC RECORDS AVAILABLE.
      This municipality shall make available to any person for inspection or
copying all public records unless otherwise exempted by state law.
   Statutory reference:
      Inspection of public records, see W. Va. Code §§ 29B-1-1 et seq.
   (C)   If a section of this code is derived from the previous code of
ordinances of the town as published and subsequently amended, the previous code
section number shall be indicated in the history by “(Prior Code, §      ).”
§ 10.09 SEVERABILITY.
   Each section of this code, including the codes and ordinances adopted by
reference, is hereby declared to be separable and severable, and the invalidity
of any section, part, paragraph, sentence, phrase or work in this code shall
not affect the validity of any other part of said code, and only any part
declared to be invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction shall be deleted
therefrom.
(Ord. passed 10-2-1983)
§ 10.10 POWERS AND DUTIES WITH RESPECT TO ORDINANCES AND ORDINANCE PROCEDURES.
   (A)   To carry into effect the powers and authority conferred upon any
municipality or its governing body by the provisions of this chapter or any
past or future act of the legislature of the state, the governing body has
plenary power and authority to:
      (1)   Make and pass all needful ordinances, orders, bylaws, acts,
resolutions, rules and regulations not contrary to the constitution and laws of
this state; and
      (2)   Prescribe reasonable penalties for violation of its ordinances,
orders, bylaws, acts, resolutions, rules and regulations in the form of fines,
forfeitures and confinement in the county or regional jail or the place of
confinement in the town, if there is one, for a term not exceeding 30 days.
   (B)   The fines, forfeitures and confinement shall be recovered, imposed or
enforced under the judgment of the Mayor or the individual lawfully exercising
the Mayor’s functions, or the Police Court Judge or Municipal Court Judge, if
there is one, and may be suspended upon reasonable conditions as may be imposed
by the Mayor, other authorized individual or Judge.
   (C)   The town may also maintain a civil action in the name of the town in
the Circuit Court of the county in which the municipality or the major portion
of the territory of the municipality is located to obtain an injunction to
compel compliance with, or to enjoin a violation or threatened violation of,
any ordinance of the municipality, and the Circuit Court has jurisdiction to
grant the relief sought. A certified transcript of a judgment for a fine
rendered by a municipal court may be filed in the office of the Clerk of the
Circuit Court and docketed in the judgment lien book kept in the office of the
Clerk of the County Commission in the same manner and with the same effect as
the filing and docketing of a certified transcript of judgment rendered by a
magistrate court as provided for in W. Va. Code § 50-6-2. The judgment shall
include costs assessed against the defendant.
   (D)   In addition to any other costs which may be lawfully imposed, an
additional cost shall be imposed in an amount of not less than $42 for a
traffic offense constituting a moving violation, regardless of whether the
penalty for the violation provides for a period of incarceration, and for any
other offense for which the ordinance prescribing the offense provides for a
period of incarceration. Of the $42 imposed as an additional cost, $2 are
administrative costs, to be retained by the municipality, and $40 shall be paid
into the Regional Jail and Correctional Facility Development Fund in the State
Treasury in accordance with division (A)(1) above.
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see W. Va. Code § 8-11-1
§ 10.11 PRINTED COPIES CERTIFIED MAY BE READ IN EVIDENCE.
   Any printed copy of this code certified prior to the facsimile signature of
the Town Recorder shall be held to be a true and correct copy of such
codification and may be read in evidence in the Town Court without further
proof of the provisions contained therein.
(Ord. passed 10-2-1983)
§ 10.12 CODE COPIES AVAILABLE IN RECORDER’S OFFICE.
   Three copies of this code, maintained currently up to date, shall be kept
available in the Recorder’s office (hereinafter used to include and mean Clerk)
for public use and inspection at all reasonable times.
(Ord. passed 10-2-1983)
§ 10.99 GENERAL PENALTY.
   Wherever in this code, including the codes and ordinances adopted by
reference, any act is prohibited or is made or declared to be unlawful or an
offense or a misdemeanor, or wherever in this code the doing of any act is
required or the failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful, the violation
of any such provision of this code shall be punishable by a fine of not more
than $200 for each separate violation; provided, however, that the infliction
of a fine under the provisions of this section shall not prevent the revocation
of any permit or license or the taking of other punitive or remedial action
where called for or permitted under the provisions of this code or other
applicable law.
(Ord. passed 10-2-1983)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 30.01 MAYOR.
   The Mayor shall have general supervision of all the affairs of the
municipality and may require such reports from the various officers and
employees of the municipality as he or she may reasonably deem necessary to
carry out his or her executive responsibilities.
(Prior Code, § 1-301)
§ 30.02 RECORDER OR CLERK; BOND AND DUTIES.
   (A)   Bond. The Recorder or Clerk shall be bonded in the sum of $5,000 with
surety acceptable to the governing body before assuming the duties of this
office.
(Prior Code, § 1-401)
   (B)   Keeping minutes and the like. The Recorder or Clerk shall keep the
minutes of all meetings of the governing body and shall preserve the original
copy of all ordinances in a separate ordinance book.
(Prior Code, § 1-402)
   (C)   General administrative duties and the like.
      (1)   The Recorder or Clerk shall perform all administrative duties for
the governing body and for the municipality which are not expressly assigned by
the town ordinances or this code to another corporate officer. He or she shall
also have custody of and be responsible for maintaining all corporate bonds,
records and papers in such fireproof vault or safe as the municipality shall
provide.
      (2)   In the absence from the town of, or in case of the sickness of, the
Mayor or during any vacancy in the office of mayor, the Recorder or Clerk shall
perform the duties of the Mayor and be vested with all his or her powers.
(Prior Code, § 1-403)
§ 30.03 RECORDS KEPT BY TOWN COUNCIL.
   The Council shall keep or cause to be kept and preserved in the custody of
reliable persons its records as follows:
   (A)   A well-bound and indexed book called the “Lost Creek Code of
Ordinances,” in which shall be kept up to date the general ordinances passed
and adopted by the Council;
   (B)   A well-bound and indexed book called the “Minutes of the Town of Lost
Creek,” in which shall be kept up to date all the proceedings, special
ordinances or orders and resolutions passed and adopted by the Council, both of
which books shall be open to inspection by the public at reasonable hours;
   (C)   A well-bound and indexed book called the “Docket” shall be kept up to
date in the office of the Mayor, in which shall be noted each case brought
before or tried by him or her, together with the proceedings therein, the
return, the fact of appearance or nonappearance, the posting of bond, the
defense, the hearing, the judgment, the costs, and in case the judgment be one
of conviction, the amount in payment of or on the same, and the disposition of
the bond and any appeal shall be noted. The record of each case shall be signed
by the Mayor;
   (D)   A well-bound, three-column book called the “Ledger” shall be kept up
to date, in which shall be entered all amounts received by the town or which
the town pays out, with dates of such receipts or payments, and from, to whom
and for what purpose, and shall be kept in such a manner that it will show in
the third column the financial condition of the town expressed as a credit
balance or a deficit. This book shall be kept available and shall be laid
before the Council at every regular meeting; and
   (E)   Any correspondences or copies of correspondences of such a nature that
should be preserved shall be kept, and checkbook stubs, letter files and
receipt files, and such other records as the Council may designate from time to
time, shall be kept.
(Prior Code, § 1-202)
§ 30.04 COMPENSATION OF MUNICIPAL AUTHORITIES.
   (A)   Salaries of the municipal authorities of the town shall be as follows.
      (1)   The salary of the Mayor shall be $550 per month, to be paid the
first of each month, for the duties performed as Mayor.
      (2)   The salary of the Recorder shall be $150 per month, to be paid each
month, for duties performed as Recorder.
      (3)   The salary of each Councilperson shall be $60 per month, total
($720) to be paid annually, for duties performed as a Councilperson.
      (4)   The salary of Clerk shall be $525 per month, to be paid the first
of each month, for duties performed as Clerk.
   (B)   This section shall take effect, provided that no salaries under this
section shall be increased or diminished during the term of office, from and
after the next general election of the town.
(Prior Code, § 1-501) (Ord. passed 3-7-2000; Ord. passed 2-7-2006; Ord. passed
11-6-2007; Ord. passed 3-6-2012; Ord. passed 3-3-2020)
ELECTIONS
§ 30.15 TOWN GOVERNED BY STATE LAWS.
   The town government shall be conducted and administered in accordance within
the laws of the state governing municipalities.
(Prior Code, § 1-801)
§ 30.16 ELIGIBILITY.
   No person shall be eligible to the office of Mayor, Recorder or
Councilperson of said town unless, at the time of his or her election, he or
she is a resident of said town and entitled to vote in the town election for
members of the Town Council.
(Prior Code, § 1-803)
§ 30.17 CANDIDATE FILING FEES.
   (A)   Every person who becomes a candidate for nomination for office in any
town primary election shall, at the time of filing the certificate of
announcement as required, pay a filing fee to the Recorder as follows.
 
Office                                   Filing Fee
Candidate for Mayor                      $50
Candidate for member of the Town Council $15
Candidate for Recorder                   $25
 
   (B)   All money received by the Recorder from such fees shall be credited to
the General Revenue Fund of the town.
(Prior Code, § 1-809)
§ 30.18 ELECTIONS BIENNIAL; TERM.
   At the said biennial election for town officers, there shall be elected a
Mayor, Recorder and five Councilpersons, whose terms of office shall commence
on the first day of July following such election and shall be for two years and
until their successors are elected and qualified, unless sooner removed in the
manner hereinafter specified.
(Prior Code, § 1-802)
§ 30.19 VACANCIES.
   When a vacancy shall occur from any cause in the office of Mayor, Recorder
or in the Council, the vacancy shall be filled by appointment, until the next
succeeding election, by the Town Council from among the citizens of said town
eligible to the said office under these provisions.
(Prior Code, § 1-804)
§ 30.20 REGISTRATION RECORDS AND POLL BOOKS.
   (A)   Registration records. The Recorder, not less than three days prior to
every election within the town other than primary elections, shall procure from
the Clerk of the County Commission the registration records from the municipal
precinct file in said Clerk’s office which are necessary for the conducting of
the municipal election. Within ten days after the date of such municipal
election, the Recorder shall return said records to the office of the Clerk of
said Commission.
(Prior Code, § 1-811)
   (B)   Poll books.
      (1)   Every poll book shall bear on the first page thereof the following
heading.
 
Names of all persons voting the municipal corporation of the Town of Lost Creek
and the County of Harrison, at the election held on the day of ____________.
 
      (2)   Two of such poll books with the names of all persons voting shall
be kept at every election held in said town.
(Prior Code, § 1-812)
§ 30.21 ELECTION BOARD DUTIES.
   The Council shall, before the biennial election for town officers, appoint
seven voters to act as Commissioners of Election and poll clerks as hereinafter
specified, and it shall be the duty of the persons so appointed to attend at
the place of voting and to superintend the election to be held in said town and
return the results there of as required by this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 1-806)
§ 30.22 POLLING HOURS.
   At every election held in said town, the polls shall be opened on the day of
such election at 6:30 a.m. in the morning and be closed at 7:30 p.m. in the
evening, Eastern Standard Time or Daylight Savings Time, whichever shall
prevail in the community at the time.
(Prior Code, § 1-805)
§ 30.23 OPENING AND CLOSING POLLS.
   Before any voter is permitted to vote, the Receiving Commissioners of the
election shall cause to be proclaimed that such election is open. When the
polls are closed, a proclamation must be made of the fact by one of the
Receiving Commissioners of the election to the people outside in a loud and
audible tone of voice, and after such proclamation is made, no more votes shall
be received.
(Prior Code, § 1-815)
§ 30.24 VOTER RESIDENCY REQUIREMENTS.
   All persons who have been bona fide residents of the territory included in
said town for 60 days next preceding any election held therein and who are
qualified voters under the constitution and laws of the state, and no others,
shall be entitled to vote at any election held in said town, but no person
shall be deemed a resident of said town by reason of being stationed therein
for any temporary purpose.
(Prior Code, § 1-807)
§ 30.25 MODE OF VOTING.
   In all elections by the people of said town, the mode of voting shall be by
ballot, but the voter shall be left free to vote by either open, sealed or
secret ballot, as he or she may elect.
(Prior Code, § 1-808)
§ 30.26 VOTING PROCEDURE.
   (A)   (1)   Any person offering to vote in an election shall, upon entering
the election room, clearly state his or her name and residence to the poll
clerk. If such person is found to be duly registered and qualified to vote, one
of the Receiving Commissioners shall present to him or her a poll slip, to be
signed by the voter and presented to the second Receiving Commissioner.
      (2)   When the voter’s signature is properly recorded, the second
Commissioner and the poll clerk shall each sign their own names in the place
indicated on the back of the official ballot and it shall be delivered to the
voter, to be voted by him or her then without leaving the election room, and in
no case shall either of said officials sign the name of the other.
   (B)   (1)   After preparing the ballot, the voter shall fold the same so
that the face shall not be exposed and so that the names of the election
officials thereon shall be seen. The voter shall then announce his or her name
and present his or her ballot to one of the Commissioners, who shall hand the
same to the other Commissioner, who shall deposit it in the ballot box if such
ballot is the official one and properly signed.
      (2)   The Commissioners of the election may inspect every ballot before
it is deposited in the ballot box to ascertain whether it is single but without
unfolding it or unrolling it so as to disclose its content.
   (C)   When the voter has voted, he or she shall retire immediately from the
election room and beyond the 60-foot limit thereof and shall not return except
by permission of the Commissioners.
(Prior Code, § 1-813)
§ 30.27 ABSENTEE VOTERS.
   Any person who is duly registered and otherwise qualified to vote, but who
is unable to vote in person at the polls in said election by reason of illness,
injury or physical disability, or who is required to be absent from the
corporation during the entire time the polls are open in said election, may
apply to the Recorder’s office for an absent voter’s ballot.
(Prior Code, § 1-810)
§ 30.28 ABSENTEE BALLOTS.
   (A)   Voting by personal appearance.
      (1)   A person desiring to vote an absent voter’s ballot by personal
appearance may appear during regular business hours at the office of the Town
Recorder not more than 15 days before the election, and not any day thereafter
up to and including the Saturday next preceding the date of the election, and
shall make application to vote by absentee ballot. Said application shall be in
writing and shall contain the voter’s sworn statement that he or she is a duly
registered and qualified voter and giving the specific reason for his or her
required absence.
      (2)   Upon determination by the Town Recorder that the applicant is
entitled to vote an absentee voter’s ballot by personal appearance, the
Recorder shall hand to him or her one absentee voter’s ballot, one voter’s
ballot envelope No. 1, unsealed, and one absent voter’s ballot envelope No. 2,
unsealed. The voter shall then retire to the place provided in said Recorder’s
office and there mark his or her ballot. The voter shall then enclose the same
in envelope No. 1 and seal it; enclose envelope No. 1 in envelope No. 2 and
seal it; and transmit possession of such sealed envelope to the Town Recorder.
      (3)   Upon receipt of such sealed envelope, the Town Recorder shall enter
the required information into the record of the person applying for voting by
an absent voter’s ballot and shall place such sealed envelope in a secure
location in his or her office, there to remain until delivered to the polling
place in accordance with the provisions of the Election Laws of the state,
being W. Va. Code Ch. 3.
   (B)   Voting by mail.
      (1)   Any person desiring to vote an absent voter’s ballot by mail may
not more than 60 days prior to the date of the election, and on any day
thereafter up to and including the fourth day preceding the election, make
application by mail to the Town Recorder for an absent voter’s ballot to be
voted at such election.
      (2)   Upon determination by the Town Recorder that the applicant is
entitled to vote an absentee voter ballot by mail, the Recorder shall, between
the twentieth day and the fourth day next prior to the election, mail the
applicant one absent voter’s ballot and one absent voter’s ballot envelope No.
2. After the voter has voted his or her absent voter’s ballot, he or she shall
enclose the absent voter’s ballot in absent voter’s ballot envelope No. 2 and
seal that envelope, and mail, postage prepaid, said sealed envelope.
      (3)   The Recorder shall, upon receipt of such sealed envelope, enter the
required information into a record of persons applying for voting by an absent
voter’s ballot and shall place such sealed envelope in a secure location in his
or her office, there to remain until delivered to the polling place in
accordance with the provisions of the Election Laws of the state, being W. Va.
Code Ch. 3.
(Prior Code, § 1-814)
§ 30.29 VOTING ONLY ONCE.
   No person shall vote more than once in the same election, even if he or she
may not have voted the first time for as many persons as he or she might have
lawfully voted for.
(Prior Code, § 1-818)
§ 30.30 CHALLENGES.
   The Commissioners holding the election at the place of voting shall permit
all persons to vote entitled to do so and reject the votes of all persons not
entitled to vote at said election, and shall, in all respects, have the poll
taken fairly according to law. They shall swear and examine any person (or the
person examined may affirm) regarding his or her right to vote at said election
whenever such right to vote is questioned by any person. If the vote of any
person offering to vote be rejected, his or her name, if required by him or her
or by any candidate at said election, shall be entered on a separate list to be
kept for that purpose; and if any person be permitted to vote whose vote is
challenged, the word “challenged” shall be written on the poll book opposite
his or her name.
(Prior Code, § 1-817)
§ 30.31 PROCEDURES AFTER POLLS CLOSED.
   As soon as possible after the polls are closed, the names entered on the
poll books shall be counted by the Receiving Commissioners and the clerk and
the number thereof set down in words at length, and also in figures, at the
foot of the lists, which shall there be signed by the Commissioners and clerk.
The Receiving Board shall then join the Counting Board in counting, tabulating
and summarizing the votes in the manner provided in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 1-821)
§ 30.32 COUNTING VOTES.
   (A)   Commencement of counting. When the time to begin counting the votes
arrives, the County Board shall take charge of the first ballot box as
heretofore provided, and shall proceed to ascertain the result of the election
in the manner hereinafter specified, and shall not adjourn nor delay until the
votes are all counted, the result ascertained, the memorandum made and copies
thereof delivered and posted as hereinafter required.
(Prior Code, § 1-819)
   (B)   Counting procedures.
      (1)   When the Counting Board has retired to the place provided for the
counting of the votes, the ballot box shall be opened and one of the Counting
Commissioners, taking therefrom one ballot at a time in the presence of the
other officers, shall read therefrom the designation of the office to be filled
and the names of the persons voted for to fill each office and hand the ballot
to the other Counting Commissioner, who, if satisfied that it was correctly
read, shall deposit it in the locked ballot box provided for this purpose. The
contents of the ballots, as they are read, shall be entered by the counting
clerks separately, under the supervision of the Counting Commissioners, on
tally papers for that purpose by suitable marks in ink opposite to or under the
name of each person voted for.
      (2)   If two or more ballots be found folded or rolled together and the
names thereon be the same, one of them only shall be counted, but if the names
thereon be different in any particular, neither of them shall be counted,
except if it be manifest what was intended by the voter, and in either case,
the Commissioners shall, in writing in ink, place a common number on said
ballots and state thereon that they were folded or rolled together when voted.
(Prior Code, § 1-820)
§ 30.33 CERTIFICATE OF TABULATION.
   (A)   As soon as the results are ascertained, the Commissioners and clerks
of the election shall make out and sign two certificates thereof in the
following form or to the following effect: “We, the undersigned, who acted as
Commissioners and clerks of election held at the Community Building, the
municipal corporation of Lost Creek and County of Harrison, on the ____ day of
________, do certify that, having been first duly sworn, we have fairly and
impartially held the said election according to law and the result thereof is
as follows: For the office of Mayor, _____________ received _____ votes,
_____________ received _____ votes,” and so on throughout, stating the name of
every person voted for, for every office, and in words at length and also in
figures the number of votes he or she received for the same, and concluding as
follows: “Given under our hands this ____ day of ________.”
   (B)   The said two certificates shall contain complete returns of the polls
taken for every office to be filled. When said certificates are signed, the
ballots shall be enclosed by the Commissioners in an envelope, which they shall
seal up where it is sealed, and endorse in ink on the outside of said envelope
as follows: “Ballots of the election in the municipal corporation of the Town
of Lost Creek, County of Harrison, the ____ day of ________.” The ballots
sealed in said envelope shall be returned to the ballot box together with the
tally sheets, poll books and certificates, and all shall be locked therein. The
Receiving Board poll clerk shall take charge of and, within 12 hours after said
completion, shall deliver said ballot box with its contents intact, and the
ballot box keys, to the Recorder, to be preserved by him or her and delivered
to the Board of Canvassers as provided in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 1-822)
§ 30.34 BOARD OF CANVASSERS; ASCERTAINING RESULTS.
   (A)   The Town Council shall be ex-officio a Board of Canvassers and, as
such, shall keep in the minute book a complete record of all its proceedings in
ascertaining and declaring the result of every election in said town. Said
Council shall convene as such Canvassing Board at the Mayor’s office on the
fifth day (Sunday excepted) after every election held for said town, and the
Recorder shall lay the ballots, poll books, tally sheets and certificates
before it.
   (B)   The Council may, if deemed necessary, required the attendance of any
of the Commissioners, poll clerks or other persons present at the election to
appear and testify respecting the same, and make such others as shall seem
proper to procure correct returns and ascertain the true result of said
election in said town, but in such case, all of the questions to the witnesses
and all the answers thereto, and the evidence, shall be taken down in full and
spread upon the record or a transcript thereof filed and made a part of the
record. All orders made shall also be spread upon the record. The Council may
adjourn from time to time, but not longer than absolutely necessary, and when a
majority of the Council is not present, its meeting shall stand adjourned until
the next day, and so on from day to day, until a quorum be present.
   (C)   The Council, before proceeding to canvass the returns of the election,
shall open the sealed package of ballots therein so laid before them and count
the number and enter the same number upon the record. The ballots therein shall
then be again sealed up carefully in a new envelope, and each member of the
Council present shall write his or her name across the place where said
envelope is sealed. After canvassing the returns of the election, the Council
shall, upon the demand of any candidate voted for at such election, open and
examine the sealed package of ballots and recount the same, but in such a case,
they shall seal the same again along with the envelope above named, and the
Recorder and each member of the Council shall write his or her name across the
place or places where it is sealed and endorse in ink, on the outside: “Ballots
of the election in the municipal corporation of the Town of Lost Creek, County
of Harrison, on the ____ day of ________.”
(Prior Code, § 1-823)
§ 30.35 BALLOT PRESERVATION AND DESTRUCTION; COST OF RECOUNTS.
   (A)   When the Council has made its certification and declared the result as
hereinafter provided, it shall deposit the sealed package of ballots, poll
books, tally sheets and certificates with the Recorder, who shall carefully
preserve the same for 60 days.
      (1)   If there be no contest pending as to any such election, said
ballots, poll books, tally sheets and certificates shall be destroyed, by fire
or otherwise, without opening the sealed package of ballots.
      (2)   If there be such contest pending, then they shall be so destroyed
as soon as said contest is ended.
   (B)   If the result is not changed by such recount, the cost and expense
thereof shall be paid by the party at whose instance the same was made.
(Prior Code, § 1-824)
§ 30.36 CERTIFICATION OF ELECTION RESULTS.
   (A)   When an election is held in said town for the offices of Mayor,
Recorder and Councilperson, the Town Council or a quorum thereof, under the
regulations prescribed in §
30.34 of this chapter, shall carefully and impartially ascertain the result of
said election and shall record the same in the minute book in the following
form, or to the following effect.
 
The Town Council of the Town of Lost Creek, having carefully and impartially
examined the returns laid before it of the election held in said town on the
____ day of ________, the members of said Council in attendance at this meeting
do hereby certify that in said town for the office of Mayor, _____________
received _____ votes, etc.; for the office of Recorder, _____________ received
_____ votes, etc.; and it appearing from said returns that _____________
received the highest number of votes cast for Mayor, that _____________
received the highest number of votes for Recorder, and that _____________,
etc., received the highest number of votes cast for the five Councilpersons,
the said _____________ is declared duly elected Mayor, the said _____________
is declared duly elected Recorder, and the said _____________ , etc., are
declared duly elected Councilpersons of said town for the term of two years,
beginning on the first day of July ______.
 
   (B)   In said certificate shall be set forth, according to the truth, the
full name of every person voted for and, in words at length and in figures, the
number of votes he or she received for any office, and when the same is entered
on record, the members of said Council shall affix their signatures thereto on
said record. A copy of said certificate shall also be delivered by mail or by
hand to each newly elected officer.
(Prior Code, § 1-825)
§ 30.37 TIE VOTE PROCEDURES; CONTESTED ELECTIONS.
   After the votes are canvassed and the results certified, if two or more
persons shall have received an equal number of votes for the same office in
said election held in said town, if such number be the highest in said election
held in said town for such office, the Canvassing Board shall notify such
candidates to appear before said Board within 72 hours of said certification.
At this time, in their presence, the Canvassing Board shall decide by lot which
of them shall be returned elected and shall make their return accordingly. All
contested elections shall be heard and decided by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 1-826)
§ 30.38 CORRECTION OF RETURNS.
   Though illegal votes be received or legal votes be rejected, the returns of
the votes taken in such election shall not be set aside for that cause, but it
may be shown, by proper evidence before the Council, for whom such illegal
votes, or any of them, were cast or for whom the legal votes which were
rejected would have been given, and the returns shall be corrected only to the
extent that it is so shown.
(Prior Code, § 1-827)
§ 30.39 PAYMENT OF ELECTION OFFICIALS.
   Every Commissioner and clerk of election appointed under the provisions of
this subchapter shall be paid the sum of $15 for training, and $150 for the day
of election, and $50 for the Counting Board, making the total pay for election
workers $215 a person.
(Prior Code, § 1-828) (Ord. passed 7-1-2003; Ord. passed 4-5-2016; Ord. passed
6-7-2022)
MEETINGS
§ 30.50 REGULAR MEETINGS; TIME AND PLACE.
   The governing body shall hold regular monthly meetings at 7:30 p.m., hour
specified from time to time by an order of the Council, on the first Tuesday of
each month at the Community Building.
(Prior Code, § 1-101)
§ 30.51 SPECIAL MEETINGS.
   The Mayor, when he or she deems it necessary, may call a special meeting of
the Council by giving its members and the Recorder notice of not less than 12
hours next prior to such meeting, and any two members of the Council, when they
deem it necessary, may call such a meeting by giving such notice as aforesaid
to the Mayor, Recorder and other members of the Council.
(Prior Code, § 1-102)
§ 30.52 ORDER OF BUSINESS.
   At each meeting of the governing body, the following regular order of
business shall be observed unless dispensed with by a majority vote of the
members present:
   (A)   Call to order by the Mayor;
   (B)   Roll call by the Recorder or Clerk;
   (C)   Reading of the minutes of the previous meeting by the Recorder or
Clerk and approval of corrections;
   (D)   Grievance of citizens;
   (E)   Communications from the Mayor;
   (F)   Reports from committees, members of the governing body and other
officers;
   (G)   Old business;
   (H)   New business; and
   (I)   Adjournment.
(Prior Code, § 1-103)
§ 30.53 RULES OF ORDER.
   The rules of order and parliamentary procedure contained in Robert’s Rules
of Order, Revised, shall govern the transaction of business by and before the
governing body at its meetings in all cases to which they are applicable and in
which they are not inconsistent with the provisions of the town ordinances and
this code.
(Prior Code, § 1-104)
§ 30.54 PASSING ORDINANCES ON FIRST READING.
   The Council may pass any pending ordinance, other than those whose
requirements as to readings are otherwise set out in the state statutes, for
the town on its first reading before a meeting of the Council and without
posting or publication by the Council, and the same shall become effective
forthwith.
(Prior Code, § 1-605)
§ 30.55 COUNCILPERSONS REQUIRED TO ATTEND.
   When there is not a quorum present at any meeting, regular or special, the
Mayor, in order to secure a quorum, may give a forthwith notice, in writing, to
any absent member or members to forthwith attend such meeting, whereupon such
member or members so notified shall at once attend the meeting unless excused
by the Mayor.
(Prior Code, § 1-201)
§ 30.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any person offending against the provision of §§
30.15 through
30.39 of this chapter shall, notwithstanding his or her having been in custody,
be liable to any penalty or punishment for his or her offense prescribed by
law; and any person who, being thereto commanded by the Commissioners, either
verbally or in writing, shall fail or refuse to assist to the utmost of his or
her power in whatever may be necessary or proper to prevent intimidation,
disorder or violence at the polls shall forfeit not less than $5 nor more than
$50.
(Prior Code, § 1-816)
   (C)   Any person who fails or refuses to comply with the provisions of §
30.55 of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of an offense against the town
and, upon conviction before the Town Judge, be punished by a fine not to exceed
$100, and such failure or refusal shall be grounds for removal from office.
(Prior Code, § 1-201)
CHAPTER 31: OFFICIALS AND ORGANIZATIONS
Section

Commissions and Committees Generally

OFFICIALS
§ 31.01 TOWN ATTORNEY.
   The Town Attorney shall be the legal advisor and counselor of the town and
for all officers of the town. He or she shall represent the town in all courts
and all proceedings in which the town, or any town officer or employee, in his
or her official capacity, is a party, and he or she shall perform all such
duties incidental to his or her office as may be required of him or her by the
Town Council and Mayor. The Town Attorney shall receive such regular
compensation and such fees for special services as may be agreed upon by the
Town Council and the Town Attorney.
(Prior Code, § 1-1401)
COMMISSIONS AND COMMITTEES GENERALLY
§ 31.15 REQUIRED STRUCTURAL FORM.
   The purpose of this section is to set forth a structural form which may be
used in regard to enacting the enabling ordinance creating commissions. This
should address itself to the following:
   (A)   Created; composition; appointment, terms and compensation of members;
filling vacancies;
(Prior Code, § 1-501)
   (B)   Purpose;
(Prior Code, § 1-502)
   (C)   Officers; rules; meetings; records;
(Prior Code, § 1-503)
   (D)   Powers and authority generally; budget; annual report; and
(Prior Code, § 1-504)
   (E)   Duties.
(Prior Code, § 1-505)
§ 31.16 AUTHORITY OF MAYOR.
   The Mayor is vested with the sole authority to remove a commissioner from
his or her respective committee, appoint a new commissioner to a committee or
disband or add committees as he or she sees fit.
(Res. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 31.17 COMMISSIONERS APPOINTED BY MAYOR.
   The Mayor shall appoint one Councilperson of the Town Council as a
commissioner of the following committees:
   (A)   Streets;
   (B)   Parks and Recreation;
   (C)   Building and Property Maintenance;
   (D)   Marketing, Media and Promotions; and
   (E)   Fire and Law Enforcement.
(Res. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 31.18 COMMISSIONER DUTIES.
   (A)   Each commissioner appointed in §
31.17 of this chapter shall have the responsibility of providing an update at
each regular meeting of the Town Council or at any special meeting where an
update is requested by the Mayor
   (B)   Each commissioner appointed in §
31.17 of this chapter shall investigate any complaint made by any citizen that
encroaches upon the subject of his or her respective committee.
(Res. passed 7-7-2020)
PARKS AND RECREATION COMMISSION
§ 31.30 BOARD OF PARK COMMISSIONERS; MEMBERSHIP AND TERMS.
   (A)   The Board of Park Commissioners heretofore created and now existing
shall be continued. As authorized under the provisions of Ch. 91, Acts of the
Legislature, regular session, 1939, as amended, being W. Va. Code Ch. 8, Art.
21, the Town Council shall, by ordinance, provide that the Board shall consist
of five members and shall also provide that the members shall be appointed by
the Council. Of the four members first appointed after the membership has been
increased from three to five, two shall be appointed for terms of two years and
two for terms of six years. Thereafter, all appointments shall be for terms of
six years.
   (B)   The members of the Board in office on the date this subchapter becomes
effective shall, unless sooner removed, continue to serve until their
respective terms expire and their successors have been appointed.
(Ord. passed 5-5-1987)
§ 31.31 SUPERINTENDENT OF PARKS AND RECREATION.
   The Board shall appoint a Superintendent of Parks and Recreation, who shall
be a person of proved executive and administrative ability with experience or
professional training in physical education and community recreation. At the
time of his or her appointment, he or she need not be a resident of the town or
state, but during his or her tenure of office, he or she shall reside in the
county.
(Ord. passed 5-5-1987)
§ 31.32 POWERS AND DUTIES.
   The Board shall have the powers and shall perform the duties conferred and
required by general law. More particularly, the Board shall be charged with the
responsibility of providing public parks, playgrounds, athletic fields,
swimming pools and other recreational facilities and of providing an adequate
recreational program for the inhabitants of the town.
(Ord. passed 5-5-1987)
§ 31.33 FUNDS.
   (A)   The Council shall provide and allocate in the annual town budget
sufficient funds for the operation and maintenance of an adequate system of
town parks and recreational facilities and of an adequate recreational program.
   (B)   As provided by law, the Board may in its own name accept and disburse
any funds it may receive by gift, bequest or devise for park or recreational
purposes.
(Ord. passed 5-5-1987)
CHAPTER 32: MUNICIPAL COURT
Section
   
32.01   Town Court established
   
32.02   Disposition of persons arrested
   
32.03   Town Judge
   
32.04   Maintaining docket
   
32.05   Issuing arrest warrants
   
32.06   Issuing summons
   
32.07   Issuing subpoenas
   
32.08   Appearance bonds authorized
   
32.09   Bond amounts, conditions and forms
   
32.10   Imposition, remission of fines and costs
   
32.11   Disposition, report of fines and costs
   
32.12   Disturbance of proceedings
   
32.13   Appeals
 
   
32.99   Penalty
§ 32.01 TOWN COURT ESTABLISHED.
   There is hereby established a court, which shall be called the Town Court.
The Town Judge shall preside over said Court, or appointed Councilpersons.
(Prior Code, § 1-1001)
§ 32.02 DISPOSITION OF PERSONS ARRESTED.
   (A)   Unless otherwise authorized by law, when any person is arrested for
any offense other than one involving drunkenness, he or she shall be brought
before the Town Court for immediate trial or allowed to post bond. When the
arrested person is drunk, the police officer will refer to code set by the laws
of the state.
(Prior Code, § 1-906)
   (B)   Every person charged with violating a municipal ordinance shall be
entitled to an immediate trial and disposition of his or her case, provided the
Town Court is in session or the Town Judge is reasonably available. However,
the provisions of this section shall not apply when the alleged offender, by
reason of drunkenness or other incapacity, is not in a proper condition or is
not able to appear before the Court.
(Prior Code, § 1-1007)
§ 32.03 TOWN JUDGE.
   The Mayor is to handle judicial matters within the municipality, and shall
preside over the Town Court, and shall be known as the Town Judge.
Alternatively, pursuant to the provisions of W. Va. Code § 8-10-2, the Mayor
may appoint a qualified person to the office of the Town Judge. The Town Judge
and Town Court shall have jurisdiction, exercise the powers and perform the
duties specified for mayors, municipal courts and municipal judges,
respectively, in W. Va. Code § 8-10-1, as last amended.
(Prior Code, § 1-1002)
§ 32.04 MAINTAINING DOCKET.
   The Town Judge shall keep a complete docket of all matters coming before him
or her in his or her judicial capacity. The docket shall include for each
defendant such information as his or her name, warrant or summons numbers,
alleged offense, disposition, fines and costs imposed, and whether collected,
whether committed to jail and all other information that may be relevant.
(Prior Code, § 1-1003)
§ 32.05 ISSUING ARREST WARRANTS.
   In addition to the Town Judge, the Mayor and the Town Recorder shall have
the authority as herein set forth to issue warrants for all offenses committed
against this code and its amendments hereinafter adopted.
(Prior Code, § 1-1004)
§ 32.06 ISSUING SUMMONS.
   When a complaint of an alleged ordinance violation is made to the Town
Judge, or such other official as specified in §
32.05 of this chapter, the Judge may, in his or her discretion, in lieu of
issuing an arrest warrant, issue a summons ordering the alleged offender to
personally appear before the Town Court at a time specified therein to answer
to the charges against him or her. The summons shall contain a brief
description of the offense charged but need not set out verbatim the provisions
of the ordinance alleged to have been violated. Upon the failure of any person
to appear before the Town Court as commanded in a summons lawfully served on
him or her, the cause may be proceeded with ex parte and the judgment of the
Court shall be valid and binding, subject to the defendant’s right of appeal.
(Prior Code, § 1-1005)
§ 32.07 ISSUING SUBPOENAS.
   The Town Judge, or those officials as specified in §
32.05 of this chapter, may subpoena as witnesses all persons whose testimony he
or she believes will be relevant and material to matters coming before his or
her court, and it shall be unlawful for any person lawfully served with such a
subpoena to fail or neglect to comply therewith.
(Prior Code, § 1-1006) Penalty, see §
32.99
§ 32.08 APPEARANCE BONDS AUTHORIZED.
   When the Town Judge is not available or when an alleged offender requests
and has reasonable grounds for a delay in the trial of his or her case, he or
she may, in lieu of remaining in jail pending disposition of his or her case,
be allowed to post an appearance bond with the Town Judge or, in the absence of
the Judge, with the ranking police officer on duty at the time, provided such
alleged offender is not drunk or otherwise in need of protective custody.
(Prior Code, § 1-1008)
§ 32.09 BOND AMOUNTS, CONDITIONS AND FORMS.
   (A)   An appearance bond in any case before the Town Court shall be in such
amount as the Town Judge shall prescribe and shall be conditioned that the
defendant shall appear for trial before the Town Court at the stated time and
place.
   (B)   An appearance bond in any case shall be in the sum of not less than
$100 and shall be conditioned that if the Circuit Court shall find against the
appellant, the fines and all costs of the trial and appeal shall be promptly
paid by the defendant or his or her sureties.
   (C)   An appearance or an appeal bond, in any case, may be made in the form
of a cash deposit, or by any corporate surety company authorized to do business
in the state, or by two private persons who individually own real property
located within the county. No other types of bond shall be acceptable.
(Prior Code, § 1-1011)
§ 32.10 IMPOSITION, REMISSION OF FINES AND COSTS.
   All fines and costs shall be imposed and recorded by the Town Judge on the
Town Court docket in open court. After any fine and costs have been so imposed
and recorded, the Town Judge shall have no power to remit or release the same,
or any part thereof, except when necessary to correct an error.
(Prior Code, § 1-1009)
§ 32.11 DISPOSITION, REPORT OF FINES AND COSTS.
   All funds coming into the hands of the Town Judge in the form of fines,
costs and forfeitures shall be recorded by him or her and paid over daily to
the municipality. At the end of each month, he or she shall submit to the
governing body a report accounting for the collection or non-collection of all
fines and costs imposed by his or her court during the current month and to
date for the current fiscal year.
(Prior Code, § 1-1012)
§ 32.12 DISTURBANCE OF PROCEEDINGS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to create any disturbance of any trial
before the Town Court by making loud or unusual noises, by using indecorous,
profane or blasphemous language, or by any distracting conduct whatsoever.
(Prior Code, § 1-1013) Penalty, see §
32.99
§ 32.13 APPEALS.
   Any defendant who is dissatisfied with any judgment of the Town Court
against him or her, within the ten days next after such judgment is rendered,
Sundays and legal holidays excepted, may appeal to the next term of the Circuit
Court upon posting an appeal bond as set forth in §
32.09 of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 1-1010)
§ 32.99 PENALTY.
   A violation of any section of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine of
not more than $50 for each separate violation.
(Prior Code, § 1-1014)
CHAPTER 33: PUBLIC SAFETY AND EMERGENCY SERVICES

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 33.01 COUNTY HAZARD MITIGATION PLAN ADOPTED.
   The town hereby adopts the county’s Hazard Mitigation Plan.
(Res. passed 3-21-2006)
§ 33.02 NATIONAL INCIDENT MANAGEMENT SYSTEM ADOPTED.
    The town hereby establishes the National Incident Management System (NIMS)
as the town standard for incident management.
(Ord. passed 10-4-2005)
FIRE DEPARTMENT
§ 33.15 ESTABLISHMENT.
   A fire company is hereby organized for the purposes and in accordance with
the provisions of W. Va. Code Ch. 8, Art. 15, to be known as “Lost Creek Fire
Company No. 1.”
(Ord. passed 5-6-1947)
§ 33.16 MEMBERSHIP.
   (A)   It shall consist of not less than 20 nor more than 64 members, who
shall reside in the town.
   (B)   Membership in the Company shall be by election by a majority of the
members of the Company present at any meeting.
   (C)   The members of the Company may incorporate in a nonprofit, non-stock-
issuing corporation under the laws of the state.
(Ord. passed 5-6-1947)
§ 33.17 OFFICERS.
   The officers of the Company shall be a Commander and two assistants, who
shall be the sole officers responsible to the Council of the town, and such
other officers as the Company may elect under such regulations and bylaws as it
may, from time to time, adopt.
(Ord. passed 5-6-1947)
§ 33.18 FIRE CHIEF DUTIES.
   (A)   The Commander of the Company shall be designated by the members of the
Fire Company and the Council as the Fire Chief of the town and, as such, shall
exercise the powers and discharge the duties of fire chiefs and shall, with the
consent of the Council and members of the Fire Company, formulate rules and
regulations for the Fire Company and for carrying out the purposes of fire
prevention and extinguishment, shall make inspections and reports required by
law and shall do generally all things required of fire chiefs.
   (B)   The Commanders of the Fire Company shall exercise the authority of a
fire chief at all fires and shall designate any person or persons to act as an
assistant or assistants.
(Ord. passed 5-6-1947)
§ 33.19 DEPARTMENT EQUIPMENT, SUPPLIES AND MACHINERY.
   All equipment, supplies and machinery used by the Company in and about the
prevention and extinguishment of fires shall be the property of the town and
shall be housed in a suitable building or buildings by the town.
(Ord. passed 5-6-1947)
§ 33.20 UNLAWFUL ACTIONS AGAINST FIRE DEPARTMENT.
   No person shall:
   (A)   Ride on any firefighting equipment unless authorized to do so by the
Commander;
   (B)   Use any firefighting equipment, supplies or machinery for private
purposes or remove or take away any such equipment, machinery or supplies from
the place the same is kept by the town, or have any of the same in his or her
possession, unless authorized to do so by the Commander;
   (C)   Knowingly sound a false fire alarm;
   (D)   Drive any vehicle over, on or across a fire hose unless authorized to
do so by the Commander;
   (E)   Park a car or other vehicle within 20 feet of any fire hydrant or
water storage area;
   (F)   Obstruct the entrance to or exit from the building or buildings
wherein fire equipment supplies and machinery are kept;
   (G)   Park any vehicle within 300 feet of a fire unless authorized to do so
by the Commander or any police officer of the town; or
   (H)   Willfully destroy, deface, damage or injure any firefighting
equipment, supplies or machinery.
(Ord. passed 5-6-1947) Penalty, see §
33.99
POLICE DEPARTMENT
§ 33.35 CHIEF OF POLICE.
   The office of the Chief of Police is hereby established. The Chief of Police
shall be the commanding officer of the Police Department, and the Chief of
Police will be under the direction of the Mayor. The Chief of Police shall be
responsible to the Mayor and to the Town Council for the general administration
of his or her Department.
(Prior Code, § 1-901)
§ 33.36 POLICE OFFICER DUTIES.
   (A)   All police officers shall obey and comply with such orders and
administration rules and regulations as the Chief of Police may officially
issue.
(Prior Code, § 1-902)
   (B)   Police officers shall preserve law and order within the municipality.
They shall patrol the municipality and shall assist the Town Court during the
trial of cases. Police officers shall also promptly serve any legal process
issued by the Town Court.
(Prior Code, § 1-903)
§ 33.37 OFFICERS TO WEAR UNIFORMS, BE ARMED.
   All police officers shall wear such uniform and badge as the governing body
shall authorize and shall carry a service pistol and billy club at all times
while on duty unless otherwise expressly directed by the Chief for a special
assignment.
(Prior Code, § 1-909)
§ 33.38 OFFICER TRAINING REQUIREMENTS; CERTIFICATION.
   (A)   Any person who is employed as a law enforcement officer on the
effective date of this section must have approved training:
      (1)   The state’s basic police training course;
      (2)   The state’s Department of Public Safety cadet training program; or
      (3)   Other approved law enforcement training academy.
   (B)   To receive certification, the person shall make written application
requesting certification. The Governor’s Committee shall review the applicant’s
relevant scholastic records and, upon determining that the applicant has met
the requirements for certification, shall forward to the applicant
documentation of certification.
(Prior Code, § 1-910)
§ 33.39 PROBATIONARY PERIOD FOR OFFICERS.
   On the hiring of a new police officer, he or she shall be subject to a 90-
day probationary period. At the end of such probationary period, the officer’s
work record will be reviewed by the Town Council and a recommendation shall be
made at that time as to whether the officer should be retained or released.
(Prior Code, § 1-911)
§ 33.40 WHEN ARRESTS MADE BY OFFICERS.
   Unless otherwise authorized or directed in this code or other applicable
law, an arrest of the person shall be made by a police officer in the following
cases:
   (A)   Whenever he or she is in possession of a warrant for the arrest of the
person;
   (B)   Whenever an offense is committed or a breach of the peace is
threatened in the officer’s presence by the person; and
   (C)   Whenever a felony has in fact been committed and the officer has
reasonable cause to believe the person has committed it.
(Prior Code, § 1-904)
§ 33.41 OFFICERS MAY REQUIRE ASSISTANCE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully refuse to aid a police
officer in making a lawful arrest when such person’s assistance is required by
the police officer and is reasonably necessary to effect the arrest.
(Prior Code, § 1-905) Penalty, see §
33.99
§ 33.42 DEPARTMENT RECORDS.
   The Police Department shall keep a comprehensive and detailed daily record
in permanent form showing:
   (A)   All known or reported offenses and crimes committed within the
corporate limits;
   (B)   All arrests made by a police officer; and
   (C)   All police investigations made, funerals convoyed, fire calls and
other miscellaneous activities of the Police Department within the corporate
limits.
(Prior Code, § 1-908)
§ 33.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any person violating the provisions of §
33.20 of this chapter shall, upon conviction before the Town Judge or such
other officer as may have jurisdiction, pay a fine of not less than $10 and not
more than $100.
   (C)   A violation of §§
33.35 through
33.42 of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine of not more than $50 for
each separate violation.
(Prior Code, § 1-912)
(Ord. passed 5-6-1947)
