CHAPTER 72: STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING REGULATIONS
Section
   
72.01   Upon highways outside of business or residence districts
   
72.02   Prohibited places to stop, stand or park
   
72.03   Moving vehicle of another to a prohibited place
   
72.04   Parking unlawfully on private property; removing unattended vehicles
   
72.05   Parking unlicensed automobiles or any part thereof
 
   
72.99   Penalty
§ 72.01 UPON HIGHWAYS OUTSIDE OF BUSINESS OR RESIDENCE DISTRICTS.
   (A)   Upon any highway outside of a business or residence district, no
person shall stop, park or leave standing any vehicle, whether attended or
unattended, upon the paved or main-traveled part of the highway when it is
practicable to stop, park or so leave such vehicle off such part of said
highway, but in every event, an unobstructed width of the highway opposite a
standing vehicle shall be left for the free passage of other vehicles and a
clear view of such stopped vehicle shall be available from a distance of 200
feet in each direction upon such highway.
   (B)   This section shall not apply to the driver of any vehicle which is
disabled while on the paved or main-traveled portion of a highway in such a
manner and to such an extent that it is impossible to avoid stopping and
temporarily leaving such disabled vehicle in such a position.
(Ord. 8, passed 8-18-2020) Penalty, see §
72.99
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see W. Va. Code § 17C-13-1
§ 72.02 PROHIBITED PLACES TO STOP, STAND OR PARK.
   No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle, except when necessary to
avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with law or the directions
of a police officer or traffic-control device, in any of the following places:
   (A)   On a sidewalk;
   (B)   In front of a public or private driveway;
   (C)   Within an intersection;
   (D)   Within 15 feet of a fire hydrant;
   (E)   In a properly designated fire lane;
   (F)   On a crosswalk;
   (G)   Within 20 feet of a crosswalk at an intersection;
   (H)   Within 30 feet upon the approach to any flashing beacon, stop sign or
traffic-control signal located at the side of a roadway;
   (I)   Between a safety zone and the adjacent curb, or within 30 feet of
points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone, unless a
different length is indicated by signs or markings;
   (J)   Within 50 feet of the nearest rail of a railroad crossing;
   (K)   Within 20 feet of the driveway entrance to any fire station, and on
the side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station, within 75 feet
of the entrance (when properly signposted);
   (L)   Alongside or opposite any street excavation or obstruction when
stopping, standing or parking would obstruct traffic;
   (M)   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or
curb of a street;
   (N)   On any bridge or other elevated structure on a highway or within a
highway tunnel;
   (O)   At any place where official signs prohibit stopping;
   (P)   Within 20 feet of any mail receptacle served regularly by a carrier
using a motor vehicle for daily deliveries if the parking interferes with or
causes delay in the carrier’s schedule;
   (Q)   On any controlled-access highway;
   (R)   At any place on any highway where the safety and convenience of the
traveling public is thereby endangered; or
   (S)   In front of a wheelchair-accessible ramp or curb cut which is part of
a sidewalk designed for use by the general public when the ramp or curb cut is
properly marked with blue paint.
(Ord. 8, passed 8-18-2020) Penalty, see §
72.99
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see W. Va. Code § 17C-13-3
§ 72.03 MOVING VEHICLE OF ANOTHER TO A PROHIBITED PLACE.
   No person shall move a vehicle not lawfully under his or her control into
any prohibited area or away from a curb such distance as is unlawful.
(Ord. 8, passed 8-18-2020) Penalty, see §
72.99
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see W. Va. Code § 17C-13-3
§ 72.04 PARKING UNLAWFULLY ON PRIVATE PROPERTY; REMOVING UNATTENDED VEHICLES.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any driver of a vehicle to stop, park or
leave standing unattended any vehicle on a private road or driveway or on
private property without having express or implied permission from the owner,
tenant or lessee of such land.
   (B)   The owner, tenant or lessee of such private road or driveway or
private property may move, or have moved, any vehicle stopped, parked or left
standing unattended on his or her private road, driveway or private property,
as above prohibited, without any liability for the cost of moving any vehicle,
nor shall he or she be liable to the owner of the vehicle for any damage done
to such vehicle in moving it unless the owner, tenant or lessee of such private
road or driveway or private property was negligent in removing or authorizing
the removal of the vehicle. The owner of such vehicle shall be responsible to
the persons removing such vehicle for paying all removal costs.
   (C)   Any person who removes any vehicle under the provisions of this
section shall notify the state police of such action and, if such vehicle is
removed within a municipality, shall, in addition, notify the police department
of such municipality.
(Ord. 8, passed 8-18-2020) Penalty, see §
72.99
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see W. Va. Code § 17C-14-13
§ 72.05 PARKING UNLICENSED AUTOMOBILES OR ANY PART THEREOF.
   It shall be unlawful for any person or owner of any real property abutting
upon any alley, street, road or highway within the town, or his or her lessee
or his or her agent, to park an unlicensed vehicle and remain thereon 72 hours.
(Prior Code, § 7-412) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no

   (B)   Any person violating the provisions of §
72.01 of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,

   (C)   Any person violating the provisions of §
72.02 of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be fined not more than $100; upon a second conviction within one year
thereafter, shall be fined not more than $200; and, upon a third or subsequent

   (D)   Any person violating the provisions of §
72.03 of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be fined not more than $100; upon a second conviction within one year
thereafter, shall be fined not more than $200; and, upon a third or subsequent
conviction, shall be fined not more than $500.
   (E)   Any person violating the provisions of §
72.04 of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be fined not more than $100; upon a second conviction within one year

   (F)   Any person who violates the provisions of §
72.05 of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of an offense against the town

(Prior Code, § 7-412)

CHAPTER 73: RAILROADS
Section
   
73.01   Speed through town limits

§ 73.01 SPEED THROUGH TOWN LIMITS.
   Any and all trains running through the corporate limits of the town will not
travel at a speed to exceed 15 mph, or other motor driven vehicles that run on
a rail service.
(Prior Code, § 9-132) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.02 CLEANING OF RAIL SERVICE.
   Any excess wood, rails, spikes and any type of material used on the rails is
to be cleaned up and maintained within the corporate limits of the town.
(Prior Code, § 9-133) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.99 PENALTY.
   Any violation against any section of this chapter’s provisions shall be
punishable by a fine of not less than $50 nor more than $100 for each separate
violation.
(Prior Code, § 9-134)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 90.01 ANIMALS RUNNING AT LARGE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person owning or being in charge of any cows,
swine, sheep, horses, mules or goats, or any chickens, ducks, geese, turkeys or
other domestic fowl, cattle or livestock, to knowingly or negligently permit
any of them to run at large in any street, alley or unenclosed lot within the
corporate limits.
(Prior Code, § 3-101) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.02 KEEPING NEAR RESIDENCES OR BUSINESSES.
   No person shall keep an animal or fowl enumerated in §
90.01 of this chapter within 1,000 feet of any residence, place of business or
public street without a permit from the Health Officer. The Health Officer (the
Mayor or an appointed agent) shall issue a permit only when, in his or her
sound judgment, the keeping of such an animal in a yard or building under the
circumstances as set forth in the application for the permit will not
injuriously affect the public health.
(Prior Code, § 3-102) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.03 KEEPING IN CLEAN AND SANITARY CONDITIONS.
   When animals or fowls are kept within the corporate limits, the buildings,
structures, corrals, pens or enclosures in which they are kept shall at all
times be maintained in a clean and sanitary condition.
(Prior Code, § 3-103) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.04 ADEQUATE FOOD, WATER, SHELTER AND THE LIKE.
   No animal or fowl of any kind shall be kept or confined in any place where
the food, water, shelter and ventilation are not adequate and sufficient for
the preservation of its health, safe conditions and wholesomeness of food, if
so intended.
(Prior Code, § 3-104) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.05 NUISANCE CONDITIONS.
   No animal or fowl shall be kept in such a place or condition so as to become
a nuisance, either because of noise, odor, contagious disease or other reasons.
(Prior Code, § 3-105) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.06 CRUEL TREATMENT.
   If any person shall cruelly, unnecessarily or needlessly beat, torture,
mutilate, kill or overload, overdrive or willfully deprive of necessary
sustenance any horse or other domestic animal, whether such horse or other
animal be his or her own or that of another person, or shall impound or confine
any such animal in any place and fail to supply the animal with a sufficient
quantity of good, wholesome food and water, or shall carry in or upon any
vehicle, or otherwise, any such animal in a cruel or inhumane manner, or
knowingly feed a cow on food that produces impure or unwholesome milk, or shall
abandon to die any maimed, sick, infirm or diseased animal, or shall be engaged
in or employed at cock fighting, dog fighting, bear battling or pitting one
animal to fight against another of the same or a different kind, or any similar
cruelty to animals, or shall receive money for the admission of any person or
shall knowingly purchase a dog or other animal for the purpose of seizing,
detaining or mistreating any other domestic animal, he or she shall be fined
and, in the discretion of the Court, may be imprisoned.
(Prior Code, § 3-106) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.07 SEIZURE AND IMPOUNDMENT; DISPOSITION OF ANIMALS.
   (A)   Any animal or fowl found running at large or otherwise being kept in
violation of this chapter may be seized by the Health Officer or any police
officer and confined in a pound provided or designated by the governing body.
If the owner is known, he or she shall be given notice in person, by telephone
or by a postcard addressed to his or her last known address, and the animal or
fowl will be humanely destroyed or sold if not claimed within five days. If the
owner is not known, a notice describing the impounded animal or fowl will be
posted in at least three places publicly within the corporate limits. The
notice shall state that the impounded animal or fowl must be claimed within
five days by paying the pound costs or the same will be humanely destroyed or
sold.
   (B)   If not claimed by the owner within the specified period, the animal or
fowl will be sold, humanely destroyed or otherwise disposed of as authorized by
the governing body.
(Prior Code, § 3-107) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.08 LIVESTOCK CAUSING DAMAGE TO PROPERTY OF OTHERS.
   Any person living within the corporate limits of the town owning cattle,
horses or any type of livestock will be responsible for damages they may cause
to another property owner. If said livestock causes damages to another person’s
property and said person has reasonable proof of the owner of said livestock,
the owner of said livestock will be responsible for the damages incurred.
(Prior Code, § 7-422) Penalty, see §
90.99
DOGS
§ 90.20 COUNTY DOG WARDEN THE TOWN’S DOG WARDEN; AUTHORITY.
   (A)   The County Dog Warden, appointed and employed from time to time by the
County Court pursuant to W. Va. Code § 19-20-6, is hereby designated as Dog
Warden of the town.
   (B)   The County Dog Warden shall have the authority, responsibilities and
duties within the town as set forth in W. Va. Code §§ 19-20-6 and 19-20-7 and
shall further have the authority and power to enforce all ordinances of the
town providing for the maintenance or keeping of dogs or the permitting of dogs
to run at large within the corporate limits of the town.
(Prior Code, § 3-211)
§ 90.21 ANNUAL HEAD TAX; REGISTRATION TAX AND CERTIFICATE.
   (A)   There is hereby imposed upon each person keeping within the town a dog
above the age of six months an annual head tax on each dog so kept by him or
her in the amount of $6 for each male or spayed female dog and $6 for each
unspayed female dog.
   (B)   It shall be the duty of each person who keeps within the town a dog
above the age of six months to report such dog to the assessor of the county
wherein such dog is kept by him or her within the town at the time the annual
assessment of personal property is made; provided, that when any person within
the town acquires a dog above the age of six months, or when a dog kept by him
or her within the town attains the age of six months, such person shall then
report such dog to the assessor of the county wherein such dog is kept by him
or her within the town.
   (C)   Each person reporting a dog to a county assessor pursuant to division
(B) above shall pay to the assessor the amount of the head tax prescribed in
division (A) above for each dog he or she is required to report, and he or she
shall then attach to the collar of each dog the proper registration tag
furnished to him or her by the assessor and retain within his or her possession
the certificate of registration furnished to him or her by the assessor for
each such dog.
   (D)   The annual head tax on dogs imposed by division (A) above is for a
fiscal year rather than a calendar year.
(Prior Code, § 3-201) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.22 EXEMPTIONS FROM HEAD TAX.
   (A)   The head tax imposed by §
90.21(A) of this chapter shall not apply to dogs in a licensed kennel or
veterinary hospital.
   (B)   All seeing-eye dogs are exempted from the head tax imposed by §
90.21(A) of this chapter, but their owners or custodians shall annually apply
for and be issued dog license tags upon display of a proper rabies vaccination
or inoculation or vaccination certificate.
(Prior Code, § 3-202)
§ 90.23 LICENSE TAG REMOVAL, TRANSFERABILITY.
   No person shall attach a license tag to any dog to which it was not issued
or remove a license tag from the collar of any dog without the consent of the
owners.
(Prior Code, § 3-203) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.24 DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE.
   No dog, whether wearing a license tag or not, shall be permitted, and it
shall be unlawful of any dog, to run at large within the town at any time. Any
dog found running at large in violation of this section shall be subject to
impoundment.
(Prior Code, § 3-204) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.25 VICIOUS DOGS.
   No person shall own, keep or harbor any dog known by him or her to be
vicious, dangerous or in the habit of biting or attacking persons, whether or
not such dog wears a tag or muzzle, and, upon satisfactory proof that such dog
is vicious, dangerous or in the habit of biting or attacking persons, the Dog
Warden or any police officer may cause such dog to be impounded and disposed of
in a humane manner.
(Prior Code, § 3-205) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.26 DUTY UPON DOG BITING ANY PERSON.
   Any dog, whether licensed or not, who bites any person shall be taken by its
owner or custodian forthwith to a veterinarian for confinement and observation
or shall be securely confined on the premises of its owner or custodian, and in
either case, the owner or custodian shall forthwith notify the health officer
of the county wherein his or her premises is located.
(Prior Code, § 3-206) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.27 MUZZLING DOGS UNDER PROCLAMATION OF MAYOR.
   (A)   Whenever it shall be made to appear to the Mayor or Council that there
are good reasons for believing that any dog within the town is mad, he or she
may issue a proclamation requiring that all dogs shall, for a period to be
defined in the proclamation, wear good, substantial muzzles, securely put on,
so as to prevent them from biting or snapping.
   (B)   Any dog at large during the period defined by the Mayor without such a
muzzle shall be taken by the Dog Warden and impounded as provided in this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-207) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.28 INDUCING DOGS TO FIGHT OR ANNOY.
   No person shall entice, induce, urge or cause any dog to engage in or
prolong a fight in the town, and no person shall induce or cause any dog to run
after, bark at, frighten or bite any person or animal lawfully passing along or
standing in or on any street or highway in the town.
(Prior Code, § 3-208) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.29 SEIZING OR ENTICING DOGS; BRINGING DOGS INTO TOWN TO IMPOUND OR KILL.
   Except for persons duly authorized herein, no person shall entice any
properly licensed dog into any enclosure for the purpose of taking off its
collar, harness or tag; or, for such purpose, decoy or entice any dog out of
the enclosure or house of its owner or possessor; or seize or molest any dog
which is held or led by any person; or bring any dog into the town for the
purpose of impounding or killing.
(Prior Code, § 3-209) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   A violation of any provision of §§
90.01 through
90.08 of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine of not more than $100 for
each separate violation.
(Prior Code, § 3-108)
   (C)   As set out in §
90.06 of this chapter, any person shall be fined not less than $5 nor more than
$100 and, in the discretion of the Court, he or she may be imprisoned not
exceeding 30 days.
(Prior Code, § 3-106)
   (D)   Any person who violates or fails or refuses to comply with any of the
provisions of §
90.08 of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of an offense against the town and
shall, upon conviction before the Town Judge thereof, be fined not less than
$50 and not more than $100, and moreover, be liable to the injured party for
the damages sustained by said livestock.
(Prior Code, § 7-422)
   (E)   A violation of any provision of §§
90.20 through
90.29 of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine of not more than $50 for
each separate violation.
(Prior Code, § 3-210)

91.99   Penalty
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 91.01 HEALTH OFFICER.
   The Health Officer shall be such municipal, county or state officer as the
governing body shall appoint or designate to administer and enforce health and
sanitation regulations within the town.
(Prior Code, § 7-401)
§ 91.02 ADULTERATED FOOD, DRUGS OR COSMETICS.
   It shall be unlawful and a violation of this section for any person to
violate within the town any provisions of the federal Food, Drug and Cosmetic
Act, being 21 U.S.C. §§ 301 et seq.
(Prior Code, § 7-402) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.03 STAGNANT WATER.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly allow any pool of stagnant
water to accumulate and stand on his or her property.
(Prior Code, § 7-406) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.04 DEAD ANIMALS.
   Any person owning or having possession of any dead animal not intended for
use as food shall promptly bury the same or notify the Health Officer and/or
Mayor and dispose of such animal in such manner as the Health Officer or Mayor
shall direct.
(Prior Code, § 7-408) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.05 PRIVIES, HOG PENS AND THE LIKE; LOCATION AND SANITARY REGULATIONS.
   All privies or back houses, public urinals, toilets and water closets within
the town shall be constructed to meet the standards of the County Health
Department, and such privy, urinal, toilet or water closet, and all stables,
hog or pig pens, chicken houses, cow barns and dairies, shall be kept in a
clean and sanitary condition, and no privy urinal, stable, hog or pig pen,
chicken house, cow barn or dairy shall be constructed or be permitted to be
constructed and remain so close to another dwelling house so that the odors or
stench from the same will be obnoxious and uncomfortable to the occupants
thereof and render the occupation of the dwelling undesirable to persons of
ordinary sensibilities.
(Prior Code, § 7-416) Penalty, see §
91.99
Cross-reference:
   Sewer regulations, see Ch. 51
§ 91.06 POLLUTING CREEKS, STREAMS, DITCHES OR DRAINS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to dump, throw,
discharge or deposit or cause to be dumped, thrown, discharged or deposited
within the boundary limits of the town, or within one-half mile above the town,
into the waters of Lost Creek or its small branches or into any gutter or drain
within the town, or within one-half mile of the town, any dead animal or fowl
or any obnoxious vegetables, minerals or any substances, or tin cans in which
foods or liquids have been kept or preserved or any oil or petroleum; or to
dump, throw, discharge or deposit or cause or permit to be the aforesaid upon
any premises or property owned by or under the control of him or her, them or
it upon or near the edge of said streams or its branches or so near as to
permit the obnoxious substances to be washed or carried into said streams and
branches by rain or drainage and thereby tend to contaminate, pollute or impair
the quality of the water in said streams and branches in the town.
(Prior Code, § 7-414) Penalty, see §
91.99
Cross-reference:
   Water regulations, see Ch. 52
§ 91.07 SMOKE, SOOT, CINDERS AND THE LIKE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or cause the escape of such
quantities of dense smoke, soot, cinders, noxious acids, fumes or gases so as
to be detrimental to or endanger the health, comfort and safety of the public
or cause, or have a tendency to cause, injury or damage to property or
business.
(Prior Code, § 7-405) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.08 BURNING MATTER IN STREETS OR ON PREMISES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to burn or cause to be burned any
shavings, refuse, waste paper, rubbish or other matter in any street, road,
alley or highway within the town without the consent of the Mayor thereof, and
no person shall burn the same or cause or permit the same to be done upon his
or her premises so close to the dwelling house of another so that the dense
smoke, noxious fumes, gas, soot or cinders will be in such quantity so as to
render the occupation of the dwelling uncomfortable to a person of ordinary
sensibilities.
(Prior Code, § 7-415) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.09 PREMISES CONTAINING HEALTH AND SANITATION NUISANCES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to permit any premises owned, occupied
or controlled by him or her to become or remain in a filthy condition, or
permit the use or occupation of the same in such a manner so as to create
noxious or offensive smells and odors in connection therewith, or to allow the
accumulation or creation of unwholesome and offensive matter or the breeding of
flies, rodents or other vermin on the premises to the menace of the public
health or the annoyance of people residing within the vicinity.
(Prior Code, § 7-409) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.10 TOWN COUNCIL MAY CONDEMN OR ORDER PROPERTY RESTORED.
   The Town Council can condemn, or make property owners restore, properties
within the corporate limits. Such properties the Town Council feels are
eyesores, fire hazards or injurious to health and lives, in ruins or
thereabout, the landowners will be responsible for maintaining. No person,
firm, corporation or association owning real estate within the corporate limits
of the town, nor any leasee or subleasee thereof, shall suffer or permit such
real estate of any character to fall into such state of neglect or disrepair as
to be as aforesaid. If, in the opinion of the Council, such condition exists or
arises, the Council shall take prompt and appropriate legal action to cause
such condition to be corrected or abated as a public nuisance as provided in
this Title IX.
(Prior Code, § 7-421) Penalty, see §
91.99
OVERGROWN VEGETATION
§ 91.25 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   WEEDS. Includes all rank vegetable growth which exhales unpleasant and
noxious odors and also high and rank vegetable growth that may conceal filthy
deposits.
(Ord. 7-407-B, passed 8-18-2020)
§ 91.26 GRASS AND WEED HEIGHT RESTRICTED TO EIGHT INCHES.
   (A)   No owner, occupant or person in charge of any premises, or his or her
agent or employee, shall suffer or permit thereon any growth of weeds to the
height of more than eight inches, nor shall any such person suffer or permit
the growth of any weeds or grass on any part of any sidewalk abutting upon such
premises.
   (B)   All premises shall be maintained by the owners, occupants and persons
in charge thereof free of vegetation which affords a breeding place for
insects, reptiles or rodents, and upon all premises not devoted to agricultural
uses, the grass thereon shall be kept trimmed to a height of not more than
eight inches.
(Ord. 7-407-B, passed 8-18-2020) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.27 CUT VEGETATION TO BE REMOVED.
   Grass, weeds and vegetation, when cut down, shall be removed from the
premises and disposed of in such a manner so as not to create a nuisance.
(Ord. 7-407-B, passed 8-18-2020) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.28 NOTICE ISSUED UPON VIOLATION.
   The Code Enforcement Department or any officer of the County Sheriff’s
Department is hereby directed to notify, in writing by certified mail,
restricted delivery to addressee only, the owner, or the agent of the owner, of
any lot or parcel of land in the town to cut and destroy any noxious,
unhealthful or deleterious growth of vegetation and any grass or weeds that
exceed eight inches in height. Such notice shall be sent to the last known
address of the owner, or the agent of the owner, of such lot or parcel.
(Ord. 7-407-B, passed 8-18-2020) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.29 ABATEMENT BY TOWN.
   Upon the failure, neglect or refusal of the owner or agent notified under
this subchapter to cut and destroy any noxious, unhealthful or deleterious
growth of vegetation, or any weeds or grasses in excess of eight inches, within
ten days after the receipt of such notice or of service of the notice as
provided for in this subchapter, the town is hereby authorized to cut and
destroy said growth, weeds or grasses by using town forces.
(Ord. 7-407-B, passed 8-18-2020)
§ 91.30 FAILURE TO PAY CONSTITUTES A LIEN.
   The charges established by this subchapter shall be imposed upon the owner
of the premises served, and if the fee, rate or charge for any of the foregoing
services shall not be paid within 30 days after becoming due, the amount
thereof may be recovered by the town in any appropriate action; and the fees,
rates and charges for the services mentioned above in this subchapter shall, if
not paid when due, constitute a lien upon the premises served, and which lien
may be foreclosed against the lot, parcel of land or building served in
accordance with the laws of the state relating to the foreclosure of liens on
real property. The town shall file in the office of the clerk of the county
court of the county in which the premises served is located an itemized
statement, duly verified by a proper officer of the town, for recording in the
judgment lien book in such county clerk’s office. Upon the failure to pay for
such service when due, the town may discontinue such service without notice.
(Ord. 7-407-B, passed 8-18-2020)
ABANDONED AND JUNKED MOTOR VEHICLES
§ 91.45 FINDINGS.
   The Town Council hereby makes the following findings.
   (A)   The statutory provisions of W. Va. Code § 8-12-5(10) specifically
authorize municipalities to, by ordinance or resolution, as the case may
require, require the disposal of garbage, refuse, debris, waste ashes, trash
and other similar accumulations, whether on private or public property.
   (B)   The statutory provisions of W. Va. Code § 8-12-5(13) specifically
authorize municipalities, by ordinance or resolution, as the case may require,
and by appropriate action based thereon, to prevent injury or unwholesome acts.
   (C)   The statutory provisions of W. Va. Code § 8-12-5(22) specifically
authorize municipalities, by ordinance or resolution, as the case may require,
and by the appropriate action based thereon, to provide for the elimination of
hazards to public health and safety and to abate or cause to be abated anything
which, in the opinion of a majority of the governing body, is a public
nuisance.
   (D)   The statutory provisions of W. Va. Code § 8-12-5(43) specifically
authorize municipalities, by ordinance or resolution, as the case may require,
and by appropriate action based thereon, to protect and promote the public
morals, safety, health, welfare and good order.
   (E)   The statutory provisions of W. Va. Code § 8-12-5(57) specifically
authorize municipalities, by ordinance or resolution, as may require, and by
appropriate action based thereon, to provide penalties for offenses and
violations of law in W. Va. Code § 8-12-5, as amended.
   (F)   The statutory provisions of W. Va. Code §§ 17-24A-1 et seq.
specifically address abandoned and junked motor vehicles, including the
opportunity of municipal enforcement agencies, such as the Town Inspector, Code
Enforcement Officer or police officers of the town, to take certain actions to
take custody and possession of such vehicles.
   (G)   The Town Council deems the parking or storage of any motor vehicle
that has been abandoned, or which otherwise is in a wrecked, junked, partially
dismantled, inoperative or abandoned condition, upon any public property
situated within the corporate limits of the town for any period of time, and
upon any private property situated within the town limits for a period
exceeding 30 days, to constitute a violation of W. Va. Code § 8-12-5(10), (13),
(22) and (43), as amended, unless such vehicle is stored completely within an
enclosed building located upon private property only, or further, unless such
vehicle is so stored or parked on private property only in connection with a
duly licensed business or commercial enterprise operated and conducted pursuant
to law when such parking or storage of vehicles is necessary to the operation
of the business or commercial enterprise.
   (H)   The Town Council further finds that the keeping of abandoned or junked
motor vehicles reflects negatively upon the appearance and image of the
community, impairing property values and damaging neighborhood harmony.
   (I)   The Town Council further deems it to be reasonable and appropriate to
establish specific warning notice provisions for those violating the provisions
of this subchapter by storing abandoned or junked motor vehicles upon private
property prior to the issuance of any citation that could result in the
imposition of penalties, which include possible fines and the imposition of
fees, costs and expenses incurred by the town, against persons convicted of
violating the provisions of this subchapter.
(Ord. 7-423, passed 11-1-2022) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.46 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLE. Any motor vehicle, or substantial part thereof,
that is functionally or legally inoperative and that has been left unattended,
discarded or deserted on either public or private property, other than such a
vehicle that is kept or maintained within a fully enclosed building or within a
licensed salvage yard, vehicle auction establishment or licensed and
appropriately zoned vehicle repair establishment. To avoid any possible
misunderstanding, a FUNCTIONALLY INOPERATIVE VEHICLE is one that cannot be
driven from its stored location, and a LEGALLY INOPERATIVE MOTOR VEHICLE
specifically includes any vehicle that is not currently licensed, inspected or
registered, and in either case, is not kept or maintained within a fully
enclosed building, licensed salvage yard, vehicle auction establishment or
licensed and appropriately zoned vehicle repair establishment or in the actual
possession of the demolisher or repair enterprise.
   CITATION. Any written order issued by the Town Inspector, Code Enforcement
Officer or a police officer requiring the cited person to appear before the
Town Municipal Court at a later date.
   ENCLOSED BUILDING. A structure surrounded by connected and intersecting
walls, or one continuous wall, and having a roof enclosing the entire
structure, and includes a permanent appendage thereto.
   JUNKED MOTOR VEHICLE. Any motor vehicle, or part thereof, other than an on-
premises farm utility vehicle, that is discarded, wrecked, ruined, scrapped or
dismantled and cannot pass the state inspection required by W. Va. Code §§ 17C-
16-1 et seq., as amended.
   MOTOR VEHICLE. Any vehicle that is or was self-propelled, including, but not
limited to, any automobile, truck, bus, motorcycle or all-terrain vehicle
(ATV).
   MUNICIPAL COURT. The Municipal Court of the town or the Judge thereof.
   PERSON. Any natural person, corporation, firm, partnership, association or
society, and the plural as well as the singular.
   PRIVATE PROPERTY. Any nonpublic, real property owned or occupied by any
person whomsoever.
   PUBLIC PROPERTY. Any public street, alley, sidewalk or other property not
privately owned.
   WARNING NOTICE. A 30-day notice, described and set forth pursuant to the
statutory provisions of W. Va. Code § 17-24A-3, that requires the enforcement
agency to give the private property owner and the owner of the subject
abandoned or junked motor vehicle, if ascertainable, a 30-day written NOTICE,
by registered or certified mail, that the action will be taken unless the motor
vehicle is restored to a functional use and legally operative condition, or
further pursuant to this subchapter, the subject motor vehicle is otherwise
brought into compliance by proper removal or being moved within an enclosed
building.
   ZONING AND CODE ENFORCEMENT OFFICER. The duly appointed Zoning and/or Code
Enforcement Officer of the town.
(Ord. 7-423, passed 11-1-2022)
§ 91.47 AUTHORITY OF ENFORCEMENT AGENCY; JURISDICTION.
   (A)   The officers of the town’s enforcement agency, that is, the Town
Inspector, Code Enforcement Officer or a police officer, are specifically
authorized hereby to undertake all measures permitted to be taken by an
enforcement agency pursuant to the statutory provisions of W. Va. Code §§ 17-
24A-1 et seq., as amended, as thought those measures were set forth fully
herein without limitation, and additionally, said officers are empowered to
issue citations for violations of this subchapter, pursuant to division (B)
below and §
91.99 of this chapter.
   (B)   The Town Municipal Court shall have exclusive jurisdiction to hear and
decide all matters pertaining to violations of this subchapter.
(Ord. 7-423, passed 11-1-2022)
§ 91.48 CRIMINAL ACTIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to park, store, keep or maintain
any abandoned or junked motor vehicle upon any public or private property
situated within the corporate limits of the town.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person owning or otherwise possessing
private property to permit any parking, storing, keeping or maintaining of any
abandoned or junked motor vehicles upon any of his or her private property
situated within the corporate limits of the town.
   (C)   For the purposes of administering this subchapter, a separate citation
may be issued for each abandoned or junked vehicle.
   (D)   Further, for the purposes of administering this subchapter, each
ensuing seven-day period following the date of issuance of any citation
hereunder shall be deemed to constitute a new, separate offense under this
subchapter, for which additional citations may thereafter be issued.
(Ord. 7-423, passed 11-1-2022) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.49 VEHICLES ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   (A)   Prior to any removal of any permitted or junked motor vehicle from
private property only by the enforcement agency as permitted pursuant to W. Va.
Code §§ 17-24A-1 et seq., as amended, and further, prior to the issuance of any
citation authorized to be issued pursuant to the provisions of this subchapter,
there shall first be given to the private property owner or other possessor of
the private property who is not the owner, such as the lessee, and the owner of
the motor vehicle, if ascertainable, a 30-day written warning notice either:
      (1)   Sent by registered or certified mail; or
      (2)   Served personally by the Town Inspector, Code Enforcement Officer
or a police officer.
   (B)   Said notice shall provide that the removal action will be taken and a
citation issued unless the motor vehicle is otherwise brought into compliance
by proper removal, or being moved within an enclosed building, or otherwise
being brought into compliance. All 30-day warning notices shall be prepared by
the Town Inspector, Code Enforcement Officer or a police officer, and the form
warning notice shall be filed with and approved by the Town Council.
   (C)   The 30-day warning notice period shall be deemed to commence with
either the receipt date or service date of the warning notice.
(Ord. 7-423, passed 11-1-2022) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.50 VEHICLES ON PUBLIC PROPERTY.
   The provisions of §
91.49 of this chapter shall not be deemed to apply to any abandoned or junked
motor vehicle located upon public property. To avoid any possible
misunderstanding, the enforcement agency, that is, the Town Inspector, Code
Enforcement Officer or a police officer, may immediately take custody and
possession of any abandoned or junked motor vehicle kept or maintained on
public property.
(Ord. 7-423, passed 11-1-2022) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.51 EFFECTIVE DATE.
   This subchapter was deemed effective by the Town Council beginning November
8, 2022.
(Ord. 7-423, passed 11-1-2022)
§ 91.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any person who violates the provisions of §
91.05 of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of an offense against the town
and, upon conviction before the Town Judge thereof, shall be fined not less
than $50 nor more than $100.
(Prior Code, § 7-417)
   (C)   Any person who violates §
91.06 of this chapter shall be fined not less than $50.
(Prior Code, § 7-414)
   (D)   Any person who violates §
91.08 of this chapter shall be fined not less than $50.
(Prior Code, § 7-415)
   (E)   The failure of any owner, or agent of such owner, so notified under §
91.28 of this chapter to comply with such notice or order to cut and destroy
any such vegetation, weeds or grasses within the prescribed time period is an
offense that shall be punished by a fine of $50 for the first office, and $100
for each subsequent offense, and the actual cost expended by the town in the
cutting or destroying of said growth, weeds or grasses as provided for in §§
91.25 through
91.30 of this chapter, whichever is greater. Each day of noncompliance with
such order is a separate offense.
   (F)   (1)   Any person convicted of any first offence under §§
91.45 through
91.51 of this chapter shall be fined not less than $100 nor more than $200, in
the discretion of the Town Judge of the Municipal Court, plus any applicable
fees, costs and expenses incurred by the Inspector, Code Enforcement Officer or
town in the removal, storage or disposal of any vehicle pursuant to §§
91.45 through
91.51.
      (2)   Any person convicted of any second or subsequent offense under §§
91.45 through
91.51 of this chapter shall be fined not less than $200 nor more than $500, in
the discretion of the Town Judge of the Municipal Court, plus any applicable
fees, costs and expenses incurred by the Inspector, Code Enforcement Officer or
the town in the removal, storage or disposal of any vehicle pursuant to this §§
91.45 through
91.51.
(Ord. 7-407-B, passed 8-18-2020; Ord. 7-423, passed 11-1-2022)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 92.01 TITLE.
   This chapter shall be titled and cited as the “Town of Lost Creek Nuisance
Ordinances.”
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.02 AUTHORITY.
   This chapter is adopted pursuant to the authority granted in W. Va. Code Ch.
16, Art. 3, as amended.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.03 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this chapter is to protect the health, safety and welfare of
town residents by providing a procedure for identifying and removing public
nuisances.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.04 MORE STRINGENT STANDARDS PREVAIL.
   If any provision of this chapter conflicts with a provision of any other
town ordinance which establishes a more stringent standard for the protection
of the health and safety of town residents, such other ordinance shall prevail.
If any provision of this chapter conflicts with a provision of any other town
ordinance which establishes a less stringent standard for the protection of the
health and safety of town residents, this chapter shall prevail, and such other
provisions are hereby declared to be repealed to the extent they conflict with
this chapter.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.05 JURISDICTION.
   This chapter applies to all buildings and land within the town and not
wholly within the boundaries of a municipal corporation, except for:
   (A)   Buildings or land owned by the United States government or any
department, division or agency thereof;
   (B)   Buildings or land owned by the state or any political subdivision,
agency or instrumentality thereof; and
   (C)   Buildings or land owned by a municipal corporation.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.06 DEFINITIONS AND INTERPRETATION.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   COUNCIL. The duly elected Town Council.
   HEALTH DEPARTMENT. The Board of Health organized pursuant to W. Va. Code Ch.
16, Art. 2 or Art. 2A.
   MAY or SHALL.  MAY is permissive; SHALL is mandatory.
   PERSON. Includes a natural person, corporation, unincorporated association,
chartered association, general partnership, limited partnership, limited
liability company, joint venture or joint stock company, club company, business
trust or any manager, agent, servant, officer or employee of any item.
   PLANNING COMMISSION. The County Planning Commission created pursuant to W.
Va. Code Ch. 8A, Art. 2.
   PUBLIC NUISANCE. Any thing, any act, any failure to act or any occupation or
use of property which shall annoy, injure or endanger the safety, health,
comfort or repose of the public at large, and shall be deemed to include, but
shall not be limited to, animals running at large; vessels or items holding
stagnant water in which mosquitoes can breed; carcasses of animals not buried
or otherwise disposed of in a sanitary manner; accumulations of manure non-
agriculturally related, or rubbish, which are breeding places for flies,
mosquitoes or vermin; the pollution of any body of water, stream, creek, pond
or river by sewage, industrial wastes or other substances; privy vaults and
garbage cans which are not air-tight; noxious weeds and other rank growths of
vegetation upon private property; any condition of the structure, including
appurtenances, considered an attractive nuisance to children, such as abandoned
wells, shafts, basements, excavations or unsafe open structures; any structure
that is unsafe for human habitation; any that is manifestly capable of being a
fire hazard or is manifestly unsafe or unsecured so as to endanger life, limb
or property; any structure in the state of dilapidation, deterioration, decay,
faulty construction, overcrowded, open, vacant or abandoned, or damaged by fire
to the extent so as not to provide shelter, or in danger of collapse or failure
and dangerous to anyone on or near the structure and surrounding premises; any
premises used for illegal possession, storage or delivery of or trafficking in
controlled substances, or other illegal drug activity, is hereby declared a
PUBLIC NUISANCE, and all other acts, omissions to act, occupations and uses of
property which are in fact a menace or detriment to the public health, safety
and welfare, create conditions of slum and blight or effect the quality of life
for the citizens and residents of the town.
   TOWN. Refers to the Town of Lost Creek, West Virginia.
   TOWN CLERK. The duly appointed Clerk of the town.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
PROCEDURES AND ABATEMENT
§ 92.20 FILING COMPLAINT.
   The County Sheriff and the Deputy Sheriff, the chief or any member of any
county or town fire department, any member of the Health Department, the
Executive Director or any member of the County Solid Waste Authority, the
Director, Inspector or any member of the Town Council or any person residing in
the town may file a complaint, verified under oath and penalty of perjury,
alleging the existence of a public health nuisance and request that such a
nuisance be removed. Such complaints shall be filed with the Town Clerk.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.21 INVESTIGATING COMPLAINT.
   The Council shall refer any such complaint to the Clerk for investigation
and recommendation. The recommendation of the Clerk shall be in writing and
shall be returned to the Council not later than 14 days after the date of
reference.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.22 COUNCIL DETERMINATION TO ISSUE NOTICE.
   After receipt and review of the Clerk’s recommendation, the Council shall
make a determination by motion in public session as to whether sufficient
evidence exists to issue a notice to show cause why a public health nuisances
should not be abated.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.23 ISSUANCE OF NOTICE TO SHOW CAUSE.
   (A)   If the Council determines that sufficient evidence exists to issue a
notice to show cause why a public health nuisance should not be abated, the
Clerk shall cause written notice to be served upon the complainant and the
landowner or occupant to appear before the Council at a designated time and
show cause why a public health nuisance should not be abated. Such notice shall
be served as provided under Rule 4 of the state’s Rules of Civil Procedure, and
a copy of the complaint shall be attached to the notice served on the landowner
or occupant charged with the creation of such nuisance.
   (B)   The Clerk shall record on the file copy of the notice the method by
which service was made and the date of service, and if service was made by
personal service, shall cause the person making personal service to certify the
date on which and upon whom personal service was made.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.24 PUBLIC HEARING; DISPOSITION OF COMPLAINT.
   (A)   Pursuant to such notice to show cause, the Council shall conduct a
public hearing at which both the complainant and the landowner or occupant
charged with the creation of a public health nuisance, together with such
witnesses as they may produce, shall have an opportunity to be fully heard.
   (B)   A continuance of such hearing may be granted at the instance of either
party for proper cause shown.
   (C)   If the Council determines after such hearing that a public nuisance
exists which should be abated, it shall issue an order which shall require that
the landowner or occupant charged with the duty to remove such nuisance shall
do so not later than ten days after the date such order is entered.
   (D)   Such order shall be served upon the landowner or occupant charged with
the duty to remove such nuisance by the Clerk and shall be by United States
certified mail, postage prepaid, return receipt requested.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
§ 92.25 ABATEMENT OF NUISANCE INJUNCTION.
   The Council may apply to the Municipal Judge of the town for an injunction
to abate such nuisance if the landowner or occupant charged with the duty to
remove such nuisance does not do so within ten days after the date the Council
enters as order to remove such nuisance.
(Ord. passed 7-7-2020)
CHAPTER 93: FIRE PREVENTION AND PROTECTION
Section
Fireworks
   
93.01   Definition
   
93.02   Displays require permit, bond, proof of financial responsibility
   
93.03   Days and times of allowed use
 
   
93.99   Penalty
FIREWORKS
§ 93.01 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   FIREWORKS.
      (1)   Any combustible or explosive composition, or any substance or
combination of substances or articles prepared for the purpose of producing a
visible or an audible effect by combustion, explosion, deflagration or
detonation, and shall include blank cartridges, toy pistols, toy cannons, toy
canes or toy guns in which explosives are used, the type of unmanned balloons
which require fire underneath to propel the same, firecrackers, torpedoes,
skyrockets, Roman candles, day-go bombs or other FIREWORKS of like construction
and any FIREWORKS containing any explosive or flammable compound or any tablets
or other devices containing any explosive substance.
      (2)   The term FIREWORKS shall not include model rockets and model rocket
engines designed, sold and used for the purpose of propelling recoverable aero
models and shall not include toy pistols, toy canes, toy guns or other devices
in which paper or plastic caps manufactured in accordance with United States
Department of Transportation regulations for the packing and shipping of toy
paper or plastic caps are used and toy paper or plastic caps manufactured as
provided therein, the sale and use of which shall be permitted at all times.
Each package containing toy paper or plastic caps offered for retail sale shall
be labeled to indicate the maximum explosive content per cap.
      (3)   The following sparklers and novelties shall not be considered
FIREWORKS and require a business registration fee be paid to be authorized to
sell, as provided in W. Va. Code § 11-12-86:
         (a)   Explosive caps designed to be fired in toy pistols, provided
that the explosive mixture of the caps shall not exceed one-fourth of a grain
for each cap;
         (b)   Snakes and glow worms composed of pressed pellets of a
pyrotechnic mixture that produce a large, snake-like ash when burning;
         (c)   Smoke devices consisting of a tube or sphere containing a
pyrotechnic mixture that produces white or colored smoke;
         (d)   Trick noisemakers which produce a small report designed to
surprise the user, and which include:
            1.   A PARTY POPPER, which is a small plastic or paper item
containing not in excess of one-fourth of a grain of explosive mixture. A
string protruding from the device is pulled to activate the device, expelling
paper streamers and producing a small report;
            2.   A SNAPPER or DROP-POP, which is a small, paper-wrapped item
containing not more than one-fourth of a grain of explosive mixture coated on
small bits of sand. When dropped, the device produces a small report; and
            3.   A STRING POPPER, which is a small tube containing not in
excess of one-fourth of a grain of explosive mixture with a string protruding
from both ends. The strings are pulled to activate the friction-sensitive
mixture, producing a small report.
         (e)   Wire sparklers consisting of a wire or stick coated with a
nonexplosive pyrotechnic mixture that produces a shower of sparks upon
ignition. These items must not exceed 100 grams of mixture per item; and
         (f)   Other sparkling devices which emit showers of sparks and
sometimes a whistling or crackling effect when burning, do not detonate or
explode, are handheld or ground-based, cannot propel themselves through the air
and contain not more than 75 grams of chemical compound per tube or not more
than a total of 200 grams if multiple tubes are used; provided, that sparklers
and sparkler devices as provided for herein shall not be sold to anyone below
the age of 16 years old.
(Ord. 9-135, passed 10-11-2022) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.02 DISPLAYS REQUIRE PERMIT, BOND, PROOF OF FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY.
   (A)   Except as hereinafter provided, no person, firm, copartnership or
corporation shall offer for sale, possess, expose for sale, sell at retail,
keep with intent to sell at retail or use or explode any fireworks; provided,
permits for the supervised display of fireworks may be granted upon application
to the state’s Fire Marshal and after approval of the Police Chief and Fire
Chief and the filing of a bond by the applicant as provided hereinafter. Every
such display shall be handled by a competent operator licensed or certified as
to competency by the state’s Fire Marshal and shall be of such composition,
character and so located, discharged or fired as, in the opinion of the Fire
Chief, after proper inspection, and of the Police Chief shall not be hazardous
to property or endanger any person or persons. After such privilege shall have
been granted, the sale, possession, use and distribution of fireworks for such
display shall be lawful for that purpose only. No permit granted hereunder
shall be transferable.
   (B)   The Mayor shall require a bond from the licensee in a sum not less
than $1,000, conditioned on compliance with the provisions of this section and
W. Va. Code § 15A-11-3 and the regulations of the state’s Fire Commission;
provided, that the municipality shall not be required to file such bond.
   (C)   Before any permit for a pyrotechnic display shall be issued, the
person, firm or corporation making application therefor shall furnish proof of
financial responsibility to satisfy claims for damages to property or personal
injuries arising out of any act or omission on the part of such person, firm or
corporation, or any agent or employee thereof, in such amount, character and
form as the state’s Fire Marshal determines to be necessary for the protection
of the public.
(Ord. 9-135, passed 10-11-2022) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.03 DAYS AND TIMES OF ALLOWED USE.
   (A)   (1)   The use of projectile fireworks shall be limited to Independence
Day (as well as the Saturday before and the Saturday after Independence Day),
Labor Day and Memorial Day from 11:00 a.m. until 11:00 p.m. and on New Year’s
Eve from 11:00 a.m. until 12:30 a.m. on New Year’s Day.
      (2)   Further, the celebration of Independence Day will permit the use of
fireworks on July 1 (or July 2 as the rain date) for the sole purpose of any
festival or celebration held by the town.
   (B)   This section applies to individuals as well as firms, businesses,
copartnerships and corporations, and includes, but is not limited to, all
residents and visitors of the town.
(Ord. 9-135, passed 10-11-2022) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any person, firm, copartnership or corporation found to be in
violation of §
93.02 of this chapter shall be issued a fine of $75, plus all court costs
associated with said fine.
   (C)   (1)   Any individual, firm, business, copartnership or corporation in
violation of §
93.03 of this chapter is subject to the following schedule of fines.
 
Offense Number Fine
First offense  $50
Second offense $100
Third offense  $150
 
      (2)   Any and all court costs associated with a violation of §
93.03 of this chapter are to be borne by the offending party.
(Ord. 9-135, passed 10-11-2022)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 110.01 CONDITIONS PRECEDENT TO DOING BUSINESS IN TOWN.
   Payment in full of the proper tax or fee as required by the town, the
issuance of a municipal business license and the fulfillment of all terms and
conditions of such grant shall be precedent to the transaction of any business,
profession, calling, vocation, activity, trade or employment for which a
license is required.
(Prior Code, § 5-101) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.02 APPLICATION FOR LICENSE; PAYMENT OF TAX; ISSUANCE.
   (A)   Each applicant for a municipal business license shall make an
application to the Town Recorder written and signed by hand. All businesses
within the town shall display a state certificate or license to the Recorder at
the time of making an application for a municipal business license.
   (B)   Upon the payment of such license, a tax or fee may be imposed by this
chapter, or elsewhere in this code or other ordinance, upon the municipal
business license for which the application is made.
   (C)   The Recorder shall issue the license applied for, provided that the
application is in proper form and that all requirements of state law, this
Title XI and other ordinances, and all conditions precedent to the issuance of
said license, appear to the Recorder to have been complied with; and provided
further, the application for licenses which are required to be issued by the
Town Council shall be referred by the Town Recorder to the Town Council at its
next meeting succeeding the date of filing thereof, and he or she shall not
issue any such license until authorized to do so by the Town Council, and in
any such case, the payment of any license tax or fee shall be deferred until
such application has been approved by the Town Council.
(Prior Code, § 5-102) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021)
§ 110.03 RECORDS MAINTAINED BY RECORDER.
   The Recorder shall maintain on file all applications for municipal business
licenses and a record of each license issued, which shall set forth:
   (A)   The name and business address of the licensee;
   (B)   The date of issuance and the term for which issued;
   (C)   The type of license;
   (D)   The amount of license tax to be paid;
   (E)   The number of the license; and
   (F)   Such additional information as may be pertinent to establish that all
requirements of law and ordinance have been complied with.
(Prior Code, § 5-102) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021)
§ 110.04 FALSE STATEMENTS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly make any false statement in
any application for a municipal business license or on any tax return, report
or other statement relating to any activity licensed by the town and which is
required to be made to any town officer or agency.
(Prior Code, § 5-103) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.05 CONFIDENTIAL NATURE OF RETURNS; LIMITATIONS ON DIVULGING INFORMATION.
   All returns and tax statements made by taxpayers to the town officers shall
be regarded as confidential and, except in compliance with judicial order, or
as may be required by the proper administration hereof, the Recorder, his or
her agents and employees and former Town Recorders, agents and employees shall
not divulge facts and information obtained in the administration of this code.
(Prior Code, § 5-104) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.06 SEPARATE LICENSE FOR EACH FIXED PLACE AND CLASS OF BUSINESS.
   Except as may be provided otherwise in this Title XI or other ordinance, any
person who, at more than one fixed place of business within the town, engages
in or prosecutes any business, profession, calling or vocation for which a
municipal business license is required shall obtain a separate license and pay
the prescribed tax or fee thereof for each such fixed place of business and for
each such business, profession, calling or vocation.
(Prior Code, § 5-105) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.07 LICENSE YEAR AND EXPIRATION; RENEWAL; PRORATING OF TAX.
   (A)   A license year shall begin on July 1 of each calendar year and shall
expire with the expiration of the next ensuing June 30, and licenses shall
expire at midnight on the last day of June subsequent to the date of issuance
and shall be renewable annually, except such licenses for which the tax or fee
is by the day, week, month or other period less than a year, and except as may
be provided otherwise in this Title XI or other ordinance.
   (B)   The license tax or fee for an initial license upon the commencement of
business shall be in proportion to the duration of such license to the annual
tax or fees; provided, that no license for any purpose or any length of time
shall be issued for less than $2. Any licensee may assign the expired term of
his or her license to another by endorsement of the assignment by the licensee
on the back of the license to the assignee, attested by the Town Recorder;
provided, that such license shall not be transferred to any other person, firm
or corporation except by authority of the Town Council.
(Prior Code, § 5-106) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.08 DISPLAY OF LICENSE.
   Each person to whom a municipal business license has been issued shall keep
such license conspicuously posted upon or within the premises to which such
license relates. Each licensee having no fixed place of business shall carry
his or her license upon his or her person at all times while engaging the
licensed business or any transaction incidental thereto and shall display such
license upon the request of any person with whom he or she is transacting
business or of any law enforcement officer.
(Prior Code, § 5-107) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.09 LICENSE DOES NOT LEGALIZE UNLAWFUL ACTS.
   Nothing in this chapter, and no payment for or issuance of any municipal
business license under the provisions hereof, shall be deemed to legalize any
act which otherwise may be in violation of law or to exempt any person from any
penalty prescribed for such violation.
(Prior Code, § 5-108) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021)
§ 110.10 COLLECTION BY COURT PROCEEDINGS.
   The Town Recorder may collect any license tax, fee or penalty unpaid under
the provisions of this chapter by appropriate proceedings in any court of
competent jurisdiction.
(Prior Code, § 5-110) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021)
§ 110.11 PROSECUTION FOR VIOLATIONS; TOWN RECOURSE TO SEEK INJUNCTIONS.
   If any person engages in or prosecutes any business profession, calling or
vocation contrary to any of the provisions of this Title XI, whether without
first obtaining a license therefor or by continuing the same after the
termination of the effective period of any such license, or by any violation of
the terms and conditions of such license, he or she shall be subject to
immediate prosecution in the Municipal Court, and in addition, the Town
Attorney may, in the name of the town, seek such injunctive relief as may be
appropriate in any court of competent jurisdiction.
(Prior Code, § 5-112) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.12 SUSPENSION, REVOCATION OF LICENSE; HEARING UPON APPEAL.
   (A)   The Town Recorder, upon reasonable notice to the licensee, may
summarily revoke any license issued by him or her pursuant to the provisions of
this Title XI for any reason which would have been grounds for denial of such
license when first issued, for violation of any term or condition of such
license, for violation of any pertinent provision of state law, this code or
other ordinance or for the perpetration or attempted perpetration of fraud,
malpractice or malfeasance by the licensee, without prejudice to the
prosecution of such licensee by the town.
   (B)   Any person having an interest in any license so revoked and who feels
aggrieved thereby may request the Town Recorder to further investigate the
grounds for revocation and to reconsider his or her action, and if the Town
Recorder accedes to such request, he or she may suspend or reinstate the
license pending his or her final decision. If the Recorder refuses to accede to
such request, or if, upon reconsideration, he or she affirms his or her
revocation of the license, the party so aggrieved may appeal to the Town
Council, may appear in person or by counsel, may have the attendance of
witnesses, books and papers in his or her behalf and may testify in person. The
decision of the Town Council following such hearing shall be final, subject to
only such judicial review as may be provided by law.
(Prior Code, § 5-113) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
REQUIREMENTS FOR SPECIFIED OCCUPATIONS OR ACTIVITIES
§ 110.25 LICENSE AND TAX REQUIREMENTS IMPOSED.
   No person shall, without a current valid municipal business license, engage
in or prosecute within the city any of the businesses, activities, trades or
employments named in the following sections of this subchapter. The license
taxes hereinafter specified are hereby levied on every person engaging in or
prosecuting within this town any such businesses, activities, trades or
employments.
(Prior Code, § 5-201) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.26 BOWLING LANES; BILLIARD, POOL AND BAGATELLE TABLES.
   (A)   The annual license fee to keep or maintain a bowling lane or a
billiard, pool or bagatelle table, or a table of like kind, for public use,
where any charge is made for the use thereof, shall be $25, but if more than
one of such lanes or tables be kept or maintained in the same building by the
same person, the fee shall be $15 for each additional table.
   (B)   The licensee, his or her agents or employees shall not permit any
person in any manner to bet or wager anything of value upon any game played
upon such lanes or tables. Such licensee, his or her agents or employees shall
not permit anyone to bring any intoxicating liquors of any kind into such
building or other place where such lanes or tables are located.
   (C)   Persons keeping or maintaining billiard, pool or bagatelle tables, or
other tables of like kind, in an establishment where intoxicating liquor or
nonintoxicating beer is sold shall not permit persons under the age of 21 years
to play at such tables or to remain or loiter in the room where such tables are
located.
(Prior Code, § 5-202) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.27 COIN-OPERATED DEVICES AND VENDING MACHINES.
   (A)   Persons owning and operating coin-operated merchandise, service,
amusement or music devices or vending machines shall obtain annual licenses and
pay the fees prescribed in this section on or before July 1 of each year.
   (B)   The liability for the licensee to operate any type of coin-operated
merchandise, service, amusement or music device or vending machine shall be
upon the owner of the machine. The leasing of such machine shall not be
considered as a transfer of ownership of the machine, and where a lessor-lessee
relationship exists, the lessor shall be liable for the applicable license and
fees.
   (C)   The owner of such machines shall identify each machine by installing
on each device an identification label, plainly legible and visible, in such a
manner that the machine need not be moved to observe the identification label,
and the identification label shall contain the name of the owner, his or her
telephone number, town license number and address.
   (D)   The annual license fee to own and operate any type of coin-operated
merchandise, service, amusement or music device or vending machine shall be a
flat fee of $250.
   (E)   The fee herein prescribed is on an annual basis, commencing on July 1
of each year and expiring the following year on June 30 at midnight, and is not
prorated if obtained during the license year, nor shall fees paid be refundable
if a license is revoked or suspended or business ceases during the license
year.
   (F)   The provisions of this section shall not be applicable to any pay
telephone, postage stamp vending machine or currency-changing machine operated
on the coin-in-slot principle.
   (G)   Except where the principal business of the operation of the store is
the operation of such machines or devices, no license fee shall be required of
persons keeping or maintaining such machines or devices owned by them in their
own licensed stores; provided, that any person exempt from such license shall
obtain from the Town Recorder a license receipt, at a cost not to exceed $250,
showing that he or she is so exempt, which shall be effective for the period as
provided for annual licenses in this chapter, but to obtain such license
receipt or other evidence of exemption, he or she shall make an affidavit and
produce such other evidence as to the facts entitling him or her to such
exemption as the Town Recorder, in his or her discretion, may require, which
shall be on a form to be prescribed by the Recorder.
   (H)   The proprietor or owner of the business conducted in the place where
any such machine is kept or maintained is liable for the payment of such
license fee, and upon his or her refusal or failure to pay such fee, the
Recorder or his or her agents may take such machine or device into possession
and deliver it to law enforcement officials, or law enforcement on their own
initiative or upon order or device shall impound such devices until such
license fee is paid; in the event the license fee and penalties are not paid
within ten days and after the date of such impounding, then law enforcement
officials shall sell such machine or device in the manner provided by law for
the sale of personal property for taxes and from the proceeds thereof shall
discharge and pay the license fee due on such machine or device and his or her
costs, including the costs of impounding, storage, penalties and other fees due
to the town, and the balance, if any there is, shall be forfeited to the town.
(Prior Code, § 5-203) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.28 CONTRACTORS.
   Any person, firm or corporation doing any form of construction on any
properties within the corporate limits of the town shall be required to
purchase a contractor’s license from the Town Recorder at the fee of $2 per
$100.
(Prior Code, § 4-804) (Ord. passed 1-19-2021) Penalty, see §
110.99
§ 110.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   (1)   Any person engaging in or prosecuting any business, professional
calling or vocation contrary to the provisions of §§
110.01 through
110.12 of this chapter, whether without obtaining a municipal business license
therefor before commencing the same or by continuing the same after the
termination of the effective period of any such municipal business license,
may, in addition to paying the prescribed license tax or fee, be liable for a
penalty of $50 for each year or fraction thereof during which has been a
default of such payment.
(Prior Code, § 5-109)
      (2)   Except as may herein be expressly provided otherwise, any person
violating any provisions under §§
110.01 through
110.12 of this chapter shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined not less than
$50 nor more than $200, or imprisoned not more than 30 days, or both fined and
imprisoned, and each day or part thereof that any violation shall continue
shall be deemed to constitute a distinct and separate offense and shall be
punished accordingly.
(Prior Code, § 5-111)
   (C)   Any person who knowingly violates §
110.28 of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of an offense against the town,
and upon conviction before the Town Court, shall be fined not less than $50 and
nor more than $100 for each separate violation.
(Prior Code, § 4-805)
(Ord. passed 1-19-2021)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 111.01 DEFINITIONS; EXCLUSION.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this chapter, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      GENERAL STORE. Includes any store or stores, or any mercantile
establishment or establishments, in which goods, wares or merchandise of any
kind are purchased, ordered, sold or offered for sale, either at retail or
wholesale.
      PERSON. Includes any group or combination acting as a unit, individual,
committee, guardian, trustee, executor, administrator, partnership,
copartnership, joint venture, association, trust, firm or corporation, either
domestic or foreign, which is controlled or directed by one management or
association of ultimate management.
      SPECIAL STORE. Includes any store or stores of any mercantile
establishment or establishments in which goods, wares or merchandise of any
kind, except cigarettes, tobacco products and soft drinks, are purchased, sold
or offered for sale, either at retail or wholesale, and which contains no coin-
operated device or devices owned and operated by the store proprietor.
   (B)   Exclusion. For the purpose of this chapter, no coin-operated device or
devices shall be constructed to be a STORE.
(Prior Code, § 5-301) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.02 LICENSE REQUIRED; WHERE OBTAINABLE; EXEMPTIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to establish, operate or maintain
any general store or special store in the town without first having obtained a
municipal business license to do so from the office of the Town Recorder.
   (B)   The establishment, operation or maintenance of stores by the following
shall be exempt from the license tax imposed by this chapter:
      (1)   The United States of America, this state and its political
subdivisions;
      (2)   Religious and charitable organizations; and
      (3)   Any person or persons engaged within the town in the business of
producing agricultural products who, individually or collectively, sell in such
store any agricultural products which he, she or they have produced.
(Prior Code, § 5-302) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 111.03 ANNUAL LICENSE TAX.
   Every person establishing, operating or maintaining one or more general
stores within the town under the same general management, supervision or
ownership shall pay an annual license tax of $20 for each such store.
(Prior Code, § 5-303) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.04 LICENSE TAX FOR HALF A YEAR OR LESS.
   Each license issued for the fiscal year shall be charged the full rate.
(Prior Code, § 5-304) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.05 EXPIRATION AND RENEWAL OF LICENSES.
   (A)   All licenses shall be so issued as to expire on June 30 of each year.
   (B)   On or before July 1 of each year, every person having a license shall
apply to the Town Recorder for a renewal for the license year next ensuing
unless such person has ceased to operate such store or does not propose to
continue operation of the store during the year next ensuing.
   (C)   Each application for a renewal shall be accompanied by a filing fee of
$1 for each license requested by the license tax as prescribed in this section.
(Prior Code, § 5-305) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
PROVISIONS BY STORE TYPE
§ 111.20 COLLECTION AGENCIES.
   Persons owning and operating a collection agency shall hereinafter be taxed
$100 annually.
(Prior Code, § 5-306) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)

   Hereinafter, a resident junk dealer within the town limits or a nonresident
junk dealer not living in the town limits shall be taxed an annual fee of $125.
(Prior Code, § 5-310) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.25 PAWNBROKERS.
   Persons owning or operating a pawn shop within the town limits will be taxed
an annual fee of $100.
(Prior Code, § 5-311) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.26 TRADING STAMPS.
   The annual license fee to pass out trading stamps through current businesses
in the town will hereinafter be $175 for each separate business by the same
person.
(Prior Code, § 5-312) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.27 LAUNDROMATS OR CAR WASHES.
   Persons owning and operating coin-operated devices, such as laundromats or
car washes, on or before July 1 of each year will be taxed an annual fee of
$250. The liability for the licensee to operate any type of coin-operated
device shall be upon the owner of the machine or machines. The leasing of such
a machine or machines shall not be considered as a transfer of ownership of the
machine, and where a lessor-lessee relationship exists, the lessor shall be
liable for the applicable license and fees.
(Prior Code, § 5-313) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.28 CIRCUSES, CARNIVALS AND THE LIKE.
   (A)   Municipalities are authorized to impose a license tax on circuses,
menageries and various other shows which are itinerant in nature and which are
not exhibited in theaters or other permanent places for public shows. A daily
license fee for circuses, carnivals and the like is $5 for each transport
vehicle, $5 for each concession stand and $5 for each skill game.
   (B)   Further, no “fortune teller” is permitted at any circus, show or
street carnival.
(Prior Code, § 5-314) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 111.29 ELECTRONIC OR VIDEO GAMES.
   (A)   Definition. For the purpose of this section, the following definition
shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different
meaning.
      ELECTRONIC OR VIDEO GAME.
         (a)   Includes games which, for a fee, allow the player to manipulate
characters, paddles, weapons or the like upon a video screen or playing
surface.
         (b)   Those particular games constituted as ELECTRONIC OR VIDEO GAMES
shall be determined in the sound discretion of the Town Recorder.
   (B)   Fee. The annual license tax to operate or maintain an electronic or
video game shall be a flat fee of $250.
   (C)   Liability; exemption.
      (1)   The lessor of such a machine shall be liable for the license tax if
a leasing or rental arrangement is involved; otherwise, the owner of such
machine shall be liable for the license tax.
      (2)   This section shall exempt public corporate bodies which are owners
or act as lessors of such games from the payment of the license tax.
(Prior Code, § 5-315) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.30 GARAGE BUSINESSES.
   The annual license tax shall be $20 to maintain and operate a garage
business.
(Prior Code, § 5-316) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.31 HOTELS.
   To keep or maintain a hotel where rooms are kept for transient guests, there
shall be an annual license tax of $20.
(Prior Code, § 5-317) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.32 RESTAURANTS.
   (A)   To keep or maintain a restaurant or eating place not operated in
connection with any hotel or tavern, there shall be an annual license tax of
$20.
   (B)   For each lunch wagon (mobile food cart or food truck), there shall be
an annual license tax of $20.
(Prior Code, § 5-318) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
§ 111.33 BEAUTY SHOPS, SHOE SHOPS, MEAT SHOPS AND FILLING STATIONS.

of $20.
(Prior Code, § 5-319) (Ord. passed 10-5-2021)
